when you say she's a programmer , she did do some , but the real thing is to have said the future is going to be much , much more than this .	當你說她是個程式師 , 她做了一些事 , 但真正的事是:未來會比這個更大 。
now , a hundred years later , this guy comes along , alan turing , and in 1936 , and invents the computer all over again .	一百年後 , 一百年後 , 這個傢伙在1936年之後 , 發明了電腦 。
now , of course , babbage's machine was entirely mechanical .	當然 , babbage的機器是整個機械 。
turing's machine was entirely theoretical .	turs機器是完全理論的 。
both of these guys were coming from a mathematical perspective , but turing told us something very important .	這些人都來自數學觀點 , 但追求告訴我們很重要的東西 。
he laid down the mathematical foundations for computer science , and said , " it doesn't matter how you make a computer . "	他把電腦科學的數學基礎設置給電腦科學 , 他說: 「 不論你如何製造電腦科學 。 」
it doesn't matter if your computer's mechanical , like babbage's was , or electronic , like computers are today , or perhaps in the future , cells , or , again , mechanical again , once we get into nanotechnology .	不論你是電腦的機械 , 或電子 , 像電腦的機械 , 像是babbage的機械 , 或電子 , 像電腦的機械 , 像babbage的機械 , 或電子 , 像電腦的機械 , 像是babbage的機械 , 或電子 , 像電腦的機械 , 像是babbage的機械 , 或電子 , 像是
we could go back to babbage's machine and just make it tiny . all those things are computers .	我們可以回到babbage的機器 , 讓它微小 , 所有這些東西都是電腦 。
there is in a sense a computing essence .	在某種程度上 , 有一種計算能力 。
this is called the church–turing thesis .	這叫做churchurchurchurchurchurchurchurchurchurchurchurchurchurch
and so suddenly , you get this link where you say this thing babbage had built really was a computer .	突然間 , 你會得到這個連結 , 你說這個東西是電腦 。
in fact , it was capable of doing everything we do today with computers , only really slowly .	事實上 , 現今我們所做的一切都用電腦 , 只有慢慢 。
to give you an idea of how slowly , it had about 1k of memory .	為了給你一個想法 , 它有多慢的記憶 。
it used punch cards , which were being fed in , and it ran about 10 , 000 times slower the first zx81 .	它用punchcads , 它會被飛出來 , 它會被飛過 , 一萬倍慢慢一千次 。
it did have a ram pack .	牠有一隻快速的攻擊 。
you could add on a lot of extra memory if you wanted to .	你可以加上很多額外記憶 , 如果你想的話 。
so , where does that bring us today ?	所以 , 這會帶我們到哪裡 ?
so there are plans .	所以有計劃 。
over in swindon , the science museum archives , there are hundreds of plans and thousands of pages of notes written by charles babbage about this analytical engine .	在倫敦 , 科學博物館有數百個計劃和數百個計劃和數百個計劃和數百個計劃和數百個計劃和數以千計的頁面 , 用查爾斯•巴布來寫這篇文章 。
one of those is a set of plans that we call plan 28 , and that is also the name of a charity that i started with doron swade , who was the curator of computing at the science museum , and also the person who drove the project to build a difference engine , and our plan is to build it .	其中一個我們稱之為 「 計劃 」 的計畫 , 同時也是我在博物館的名字 , 其中一組 , 我們計畫的計畫是要建立一個差異的工程 , 也是我們所謂的 「 計劃 」 的名字 , 也是我所謂的 「 計劃 」 的名字 , 同時也是我在科學博物館的名字 , 同時也是一位慈善機構的名字 。
here in south kensington , we will build the analytical engine .	在南肯斯頓 , 我們會建立一個分析的工程 。
the project has a number of parts to it .	這個計劃有一部分 。
one was the scanning of babbage's archive .	其中一個是嬰兒的分數 。
that's been done . the second is now the study of all of those plans to determine what to build .	這已經完成了 。 第二 , 目前正在研究這些計畫的研究 , 試圖決定要建造什麼 。
the third part is a computer simulation of that machine , and the last part is to physically build it at the science museum .	第三部分是電腦模擬 , 最後一部分是電腦模擬 , 最後一部分是電腦模擬 , 最後一部分是電腦模擬 , 最後一部分是電腦模擬 。
when it's built , you'll finally be able to understand how a computer works , because rather than having a tiny chip in front of you , you've got to look at this humongous thing and say , " ah , i see the memory operating , i see the cpu operating , i hear it operating . i probably smell it operating . "	當它開始運作時 , 你一定會知道電腦如何運作 , 但在你面前 , 你一定要知道電腦運作 , 不管你在哪裡 , 你就得去了解電腦是如何運作的 , 因為不是在你面前 , 你必須看著這件很棒的事 , 然後說: 「 啊 , 我知道電腦是如何運作的 , 我知道電腦是如何運作的 , 但 , 不管你在你面前 , 你一定能了解電腦是如何運作的 。 」

of course , he never built it , because he was always fiddling with new plans , but when it did get built , of course , in the 1940s , everything changed .	當然 , 他從來沒有建造 , 因為他一直在1940年代 , 一切改變了 。

daniel kraft demos his marrow miner a new device that quickly harvests lifesaving bone marrow with minimal pain to the donor . he emphasizes that the adult stem cells found in bone marrow can be used to treat many terminal conditions , from parkinson's to heart disease .	丹尼爾•克林森在骨髓裡找到骨髓 , 可以用來治療很多種類的疾病 , 從帕金森氏症到捐贈者 , 從帕金森氏症到捐贈者 。
biology , biotech , health , health care , medicine , science , technology	生物科技、健康、醫療、醫療、醫療、醫療、醫療、醫療、醫療保健、醫學、醫學、生物科技 。
daniel kraft invents a better way to harvest bone marrow	danielkraft發明了更好的方法 , 來抵抗骨髓 。
so i am a pediatric cancer doctor and stemcell researcher at stanford university where my clinical focus has been bone marrow transplantation .	我是骨髓移植手術 , 我在史丹佛大學的醫學院 , 我在史丹佛大學的醫學院 , 我的臨床專注是骨髓移植手術 。
now , inspired by jill bolte taylor last year , i didn't bring a human brain , but i did bring a liter of bone marrow .	今天 , 去年 , 我沒有帶出人類的腦袋 , 但我做了一張骨髓 。
and bone marrow is actually what we use to save the lives of tens of thousands of patients , most of whom have advanced malignancies like leukemia and lymphoma and some other diseases .	骨髓是我們用來拯救數以千計的病患 , 大部分的患者 , 包括血管病患 , 以及其他疾病 。
so , a few years ago , i'm doing my transplant fellowship at stanford .	幾年前 , 我在史丹佛大學工作 。
i'm in the operating room . we have bob here , who is a volunteer donor .	我在手術室裡 , 我們有一個志願者捐贈者 。
we're sending his marrow across the country to save the life of a child with leukemia .	我們把他的馬拉送到國內 , 拯救了孩子的生命 。
so actually how do we harvest this bone marrow ?	所以 , 我們要如何收集這些骨髓呢 ?
well we have a whole o . r . team , general anesthesia , nurses , and another doctor across from me .	我們有一個全部的團隊 , 一間醫護士 , 還有另一個醫生從我身上 。
bob's on the table , and we take this sort of small needle , you know , not too big .	bob在桌上 , 我們把這個小型的小型需要 , 你知道 , 不太大 。
and the way we do this is we basically place this through the soft tissue , and kind of punch it into the hard bone , into the tuchus that's a technical term and aspirate about 10 mls of bone marrow out , each time , with a syringe .	我們所做的是 , 透過軟組織組織 , 將它轉換成硬骨頭 , 將它轉換成硬骨髓 , 每次 , 每次 , 一次 , 用鼻子 , 將它轉換成硬骨頭 。
and hand it off to the nurse . she squirts it into a tin .	把牠帶到海裡 , 把牠帶到海豚 。
hands it back to me . and we do that again and again .	回到我 , 我們再一次又一次又一次 。
about 200 times usually .	大約200倍 。
and by the end of this my arm is sore , i've got a callus on my hand , let alone bob , whose rear end looks something more like this , like swiss cheese .	在我的手上 , 我的手臂上有一支手臂 , 像瑞士一樣 , 看起來像瑞士一樣 。
so i'm thinking , you know , this procedure hasn't changed in about 40 years .	所以我想 , 你知道的 , 這段程序已經改變了40年 。
and there is probably a better way to do this .	可能有更好的方法來做這件事 。
so i thought of a minimally invasive approach , and a new device that we call the marrow miner .	所以我想起一個新的裝置 , 我們稱之為 「 火箭礦工 」 。
and the marrow miner , the way it works is shown here .	此外 , 它的運作方式也顯示了 。
our standard seethrough patient .	我們的標準病患 。
instead of entering the bone dozens of times , we enter just once , into the front of the hip or the back of the hip .	而不是進入前面的前面 , 進入前面 , 進入前面 , 進入前面 , 進入前面 , 進入前面 , 進入前面 , 進入前面 , 進入前面 。
and we have a flexible , powered catheter with a special wire loop tip that stays inside the crunchy part of the marrow and follows the contours of the hip , as it moves around .	我們有一個很有彈性的電池 , 用一個特殊的電池 , 用一個特殊的電池 , 用一個特殊的線路來追蹤它移動的軌跡 。
so it enables you to very rapidly aspirate , or suck out , rich bone marrow very quickly through one hole .	所以它會讓你很快地從一個洞見到一個洞 。
we can do multiple passes through that same entry .	我們能做多次的熱情 。
and , so , very quickly , bob can just get one puncture , local anesthesia , and do this harvest as an outpatient .	很快地 , 鮑勃可以得到一支指令 , 例如 「 耐心 」 、 「 耐心 」 、 「 保持 」 的 「 不停 」 、 「 不停 」 的 「 無限 」 。
so i did a few prototypes . i got a small little grant at stanford .	所以我做了一些原型 , 我在史丹佛做了一些原型 。
and played around with this a little bit .	玩著這個小小點 。
and our team members developed this technology .	我們的團隊成員開發了這項技術 。
and eventually we got two large animals , and pig studies .	最後我們有兩個大型動物和豬研究 。
and we found , to our surprise , that we not only got bone marrow out , but we got 10 times the stem cell activity in the marrow from the marrow miner , compared to the normal device .	我們發現 , 很驚訝的是 , 我們並不只有骨髓 , 我們也發現 , 很驚訝的是 , 我們發現 , 不只有10倍的幹細胞活動 , 比一般裝置的幹細胞活動 。
this device was just fda approved in the last year .	這個裝置是fda的應用程式 。
here is a live patient . you can see it following the flexible curves around .	這是個活病患者 , 你可以看到它追隨著巨大的曲線 。
there will be two passes here , in the same patient , from the same hole .	這裡有兩位相同的病人 , 相同的病人 。
this was done under local anesthesia , as an outpatient .	這是在當地的麻醉劑中 , 作為一個專家 。
and we got , again , about three to six times more stem cells than the standard approach done on the same patient .	我們再次發現 , 三到六倍的幹細胞 , 比標準儀器的幹細胞更幹細胞 。
so why should you care ? bone marrow is a very rich source of adult stem cells .	為什麼你要關心 ? 骨髓是個非常豐富的成年人幹細胞 。
you all know about embryonic stem cells .	你們都知道胚胎幹細胞 。
they've got great potential but haven't yet entered clinical trials .	他們有很大的潛力 , 但還沒有進入臨床試驗 。
adult stem cells are throughout our body , including the bloodforming stem cells in our bone marrow , which we've been using as a form of stemcell therapy for over 40 years .	成年人幹細胞在我們的骨髓裡 , 包括血幹細胞的幹細胞 , 在我們的骨髓裡 , 包括在我們的骨髓裡 , 包括血管幹細胞 , 包括在我們的骨髓裡 , 包括我們血幹細胞的幹細胞 , 包括在我們的骨髓裡 , 包括在我們的骨髓裡 , 包括在我們的骨髓裡 , 包括
in the last decade there's been an explosion of use of bone marrow stem cells to treat the patient's other diseases such as heart disease , vascular disease , orthopedics , tissue engineering , even in neurology to treat parkinson's and diabetes .	過去十年間 , 這種病患的疾病 , 像是心臟病、肺結核和糖尿病 , 甚至在神經治療帕金森氏症和糖尿病 。
we've just come out , we're commercializing , this year , generation 2 . 0 of the marrow miner .	我們剛剛進來 , 今年 , 一代2.0公分 , 一代2.0 。
the hope is that this gets more stem cells out , which translates to better outcomes .	希望是 , 這會讓更多幹細胞變得更好 , 更好的結果 。
it may encourage more people to sign up to be potential livesaving bone marrow donors .	它可能會鼓勵更多人來參加會議會鼓勵更多人 , 來成為潛能的生存者 。
it may even enable you to bank your own marrow stem cells , when you're younger and healthier , to use in the future should you need it .	它可能甚至可以讓你能在你的家長和健康 , 用在未來 , 需要它 。
and ultimately and here's a picture of our bone marrow transplant survivors , who come together for a reunion each year at stanford .	最後 , 這是我們的骨髓移植生存者 , 每年在史丹佛大學的照片 。
hopefully this technology will let us have more of these survivors in the future .	希望這個科技會讓我們有更多的倖存者 。
physicist and surfer garrett lisi presents a controversial new model of the universe that just maybe answers all the big questions . if nothing else , it's the most beautiful 8dimensional model of elementary particles and forces you've ever seen .	物理學家和surfergarrettlisi現在提出了一個爭議性的新模型 , 可能回答所有大問題 , 如果沒有其他 , 它是最美麗的一系列圖形 , 它是最美麗的八維空間 , 它是你所見過最美麗的一系列圖形 。
physics , science , technology	物理學、科學、科技 。
garrett lisi on his theory of everything	在他的理論上 , 每一件事都能在他的理論上 。
whoa , dude . check out those killer equations . sweet .	阿拉伯 , 查出那些殺人的蛋白質 。
actually , for the next 18 minutes i'm going to do the best i can to describe the beauty of particle physics without equations .	接下來的18分鐘 , 我要做的最好 , 我可以描述美麗的美麗 , 不是宇宙的美麗 。
it turns out there's a lot we can learn from coral .	結果發現 , 我們能從珊瑚中學到很多東西 。
coral is a very beautiful and unusual animal .	珊瑚是非常美麗且不尋常的動物 。
each coral head consists of thousand of individual polyps .	每個珊瑚頭都有數千個單位的珊瑚頭 。
these polyps are continually budding and branching into genetically identical neighbors .	這些池子會不斷地擴散到基因上的鄰居 。
if we imagine this to be a hyperintelligent coral , we can single out an individual and ask him a reasonable question .	如果我們想像這是個超級的珊瑚 , 我們可以單單一個人 , 問他一個問題 。
we can ask how exactly he got to be in this particular location compared to his neighbors if it was just chance , or destiny , or what ?	我們可以問他如何在這個特定的位置上 , 和他的鄰居有機會 , 或什麼 ?
now , after admonishing us for turning the temperature up too high , he would tell us that our question was completely stupid .	為了讓溫度太高 , 他會告訴我們 , 我們的問題是完全愚蠢的 。
these corals can be quite kind of mean , you see , and i have surfing scars to prove that .	這些珊瑚可能是很有意思的 , 你可以看到 , 我有著驚人的證據 。
but this polyp would continue and tell us that his neighbors were quite clearly identical copies of him .	但這個警察會繼續告訴我們 , 他的鄰居是非常明顯的 。
that he was in all these other locations as well , but experiencing them as separate individuals .	他在所有其他的位置都一樣 , 但 , 把它們分離成分別 。
for a coral , branching into different copies is the most natural thing in the world .	對珊瑚而言 , 分類成不同的複製品是世界上最自然的東西 。
unlike us , a hyperintelligent coral would be uniquely prepared to understand quantum mechanics .	不像我們 , 一個很聰明的珊瑚會很獨特地預算要了解量子力學 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics very accurately describes how our universe works .	量子力學的數學量子力學非常準確描述我們宇宙如何運作 。
and it tells us our reality is continually branching into different possibilities , just like a coral .	它告訴我們 , 我們的現實是不斷地分裂成不同的可能性 , 就像珊瑚一樣 。
it's a weird thing for us humans to wrap our minds around , since we only ever get to experience one possibility .	對我們來說 , 很奇怪的是 , 因為我們只能經歷一個可能性 。
this quantum weirdness was first described by erwin schrödinger and his cat .	這種量子奇怪 , 他的貓咪是史蒂夫和他的貓 。
the cat likes this version better .	貓喜歡這個版本 。
in this setup , schrödinger is in a box with a radioactive sample that , by the laws of quantum mechanics , branches into a state in which it is radiated and a state in which it is not .	在這個盒子裡 , 用一種原始的原料 , 用一種原始的原料 , 用一種原始的原料 , 用一種原始的狀態 , 用一種原始的狀態 , 以一種原始的狀態 , 以一種原始的狀態 , 以一種原始的狀態 , 以一種原始的狀態 。
in the branch in which the sample radiates , it sets off a trigger that releases poison and schrödinger is dead .	在這個樣本的樣本中 , 它會被排列出來 , 它會被排除毒素和schrordinger死了 。
but in the other branch of reality , he remains alive .	但在其他的現實中 , 他仍然活著 。
these realities are experienced separately by each individual .	這些真相是透過每個人體驗的 。
as far as either can tell , the other one doesn't exist .	如同所說的 , 另一個人並不存在 。
this seems weird to us , because each of us only experiences an individual existence , and we don't get to see other branches .	這似乎很奇怪 , 因為我們每一個人都只經歷過一個個人存在 , 而我們不見得見其他 。
it's as if each of us , like schrödinger here , are a kind of coral branching into different possibilities .	如同我們一樣 , 如同我們一樣 , 像沙漠一樣 , 會變成不同的可能性 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics tells us this is how the world works at tiny scales .	量子力學的數學量子力學告訴我們這個世界是如何運作的 。
it can be summed up in a single sentence: everything that can happen , does .	它可以在單一句子中說:所有事情都可以發生 。
but this does not mean everything happens .	但這並不代表一切發生 。
the rest of physics is about describing what can happen and what can't .	其餘的物理是關於描述可能發生什麼事 , 或無法做到什麼 。
what physics tells us is that everything comes down to geometry and the interactions of elementary particles .	物理學告訴我們 , 物理學會告訴我們 , 一切都來自於幾何和互動 。
and things can happen only if these interactions are perfectly balanced .	只要這些互動是完全平衡的 。
now i'll go ahead and describe how we know about these particles , what they are and how this balance works .	現在我來看看我們如何了解這些粒子 , 以及這個平衡如何運作 。
in this machine , a beam of protons and antiprotons are accelerated to near the speed of light and brought together in a collision , producing a burst of pure energy .	在這個機器中 , 一個叫做 「 光 」 的 「 光 」 和 「 光線 」 和 「 光線 」 的 「 光 」 和 「 光線 」 和 「 光線 」 和 「 光線 」 的聚集在一起 , 形成了 「 光線 」 和 「 光線 」 和 「 光 」
this energy is immediately converted into a spray of subatomic particles , with detectors and computers used to figure out their properties .	這個能量會被轉換成一系列的物理粒子 , 偵測器和電腦用來找出它們的特性 。
this enormous machine the large hadron collider at cern in geneva has a circumference of 17 miles and , when it's operating , draws five times as much power as the city of monterey .	這位巨大的機器大型鐵粒子在一間大型的機械大型大型鐵撞機中 , 每次當它運作時 , 將五倍的電力轉換為城市的大型鐵粒 。
we can't predict specifically what particles will be produced in any individual collision .	我們無法預測特定的粒子會在任何一個體內產生任何一個撞擊 。
quantum mechanics tells us all possibilities are realized .	量子力學告訴我們所有可能性 。
but physics does tell us what particles can be produced .	但物理學告訴我們粒子能產生什麼 。
these particles must have just as much mass and energy as is carried in by the proton and antiproton .	這些粒子必須有許多質量和能量 , 由質量和能量 , 由質量和能量 。
any particles more massive than this energy limit aren't produced , and remain invisible to us .	任何粒子都比能源限制還沒那麼大 , 還能維持我們 。
this is why this new particle accelerator is so exciting .	這就是為什麼這個新粒子加速器很興奮 。
it's going to push this energy limit seven times beyond what's ever been done before , so we're going to get to see some new particles very soon .	它會將這個能量限制為1.7倍 , 所以我們將會看到一些新的粒子 。
but before talking about what we might see , let me describe the particles we already know of .	但在談談之前 , 讓我描述我們所知的粒子 。
there's a whole zoo of subatomic particles .	這裡有一整個zo的生物粒子 。
most of us are familiar with electrons .	大多數人都熟悉電子 。
a lot of people in this room make a good living pushing them around .	在這個房間裡有許多人在這個房間裡有許多人在這個房間裡充滿了好的生活 。
but the electron also has a neutral partner called the neutrino , with no electric charge and a very tiny mass .	但電子也有一個中央的夥伴 , 叫做neutrino , 電荷和一個非常小的電荷 。
in contrast , the upanddown quarks have very large masses , and combine in threes to make the protons and neutrons inside atoms .	相反的 , 大量的質量和中子 , 內在原子中有大量的質量 。
all of these matter particles come in left and righthanded varieties , and have antiparticle partners that carry opposite charges .	所有這些物質粒子都在左邊和右撇子 , 而有抗粒子在左邊和右邊邊緣 。
these familiar particles also have less familiar second and third generations , which have the same charges as the first but have much higher masses .	這些熟悉的粒子也比較不熟悉第二個代代 , 同時也比較熟悉第二代 , 同時也比較熟悉第二代 , 同時也比較熟悉第二代 。
these matter particles all interact with the various force particles .	這些物質粒子和不同力量粒子相互作用 。
the electromagnetic force interacts with electrically charged matter via particles called photons .	電磁力與電磁力互動 , 電磁力與電磁力相互作用 , 叫做光子 。
there is also a very weak force called , rather unimaginatively , the weak force , that interacts only with lefthanded matter .	也有一種非常弱勢的力量 , 例如 , 弱勢力 , 與左撇子相互相互作用 。
the strong force acts between quarks which carry a different kind of charge , called color charge , and come in three different varieties: red , green and blue .	強大的力量在三種不同的不同種種中:紅色、綠色和藍色 。
you can blame murray gellmann for these names they're his fault .	你可以怪怪murraygellmann的名字是他的錯 。
finally , there's the force of gravity , which interacts with matter via its mass and spin .	最後 , 重力的力量是重力的力量 , 與物質的力量相互作用 。
the most important thing to understand here is that there's a different kind of charge associated with each of these forces .	最重要的是 , 要了解這裡有不同的特徵 , 和所有這些力量有關 。
these four different forces interact with matter according to the corresponding charges that each particle has .	這些四種不同的力量互相作用 , 每一個粒子都有 。
a particle that hasn't been seen yet , but we're pretty sure exists , is the higgs particle , which gives masses to all these other particles .	一個粒子也沒有被看過 , 但是我們很確定存在 , 希格斯粒子是希格斯粒子 , 它會讓質量到其他粒子中 。
the main purpose of the large hadron collider is to see this higgs particle , and we're almost certain it will .	大型鐵粒子的主要目的是要看到希格斯粒子 , 我們幾乎肯定會這樣 。
but the greatest mystery is what else we might see .	但最偉大的謎就是我們所看到的 。
and i'm going to show you one beautiful possibility towards the end of this talk .	接下來我要展示給你們看一個美好的可能性 , 讓大家看出一個美妙的可能性 。
now , if we count up all these different particles using their various spins and charges , there are 226 .	現在 , 如果我們把這些不同的粒子用不同粒子用它們不同的粒子 , 用它們不同的粒子 , 兩二二氧化碳 。
that's a lot of particles to keep track of .	有很多粒子可以繼續追蹤 。
and it seems strange that nature would have so many elementary particles .	它似乎很奇怪 , 自然會有很多元素 。
but if we plot them out according to their charges , some beautiful patterns emerge .	但如果我們把它們帶到他們的荷蘭 , 有些美麗的模式就出現了 。
the most familiar charge is electric charge .	最熟悉的電荷是電荷 。
electrons have an electric charge , a negative one , and quarks have electric charges in thirds .	電子電荷有電荷 , 電荷則有電荷 。
so when two up quarks and a down quark are combined to make a proton , it has a total electric charge of plus one .	所以 , 當兩公尺長的電荷時 , 它的電荷有一連串的電荷 。
these particles also have antiparticles , which have opposite charges .	這些粒子也具有反粒子 , 相反的粒子也具有反粒子 。
now , it turns out the electric charge is actually a combination of two other charges: hypercharge and weak charge .	現在 , 電荷是由兩個其他電荷所組成的組合:hy和弱荷 。
if we spread out the hypercharge and weak charge and plot the charges of particles in this twodimensional charge space , the electric charge is where these particles sit along the vertical direction .	如果我們把這些粒子放在兩維空間的電荷中 , 電荷就是這些粒子在垂直方向上 。
the electromagnetic and weak forces interact with matter according to their hypercharge and weak charge , which make this pattern .	電磁力和弱力會互相作用 , 讓這個模式的動作和弱勢 。
this is called the unified electroweak model , and it was put together back in 1967 .	這叫做 「 非凡的電池模型 」 , 它在1967年開始 。
the reason most of us are only familiar with electric charge and not both of these is because of the higgs particle .	大多數人都只熟悉電荷 , 而不是因為希格斯粒子 。
the higgs , over here on the left , has a large mass and breaks the symmetry of this electroweak pattern .	希格斯在左邊 , 左邊有大量 , 產生了巨大的質量 , 讓它的對稱性 。
it makes the weak force very weak by giving the weak particles a large mass .	它讓弱勢力很弱 , 讓弱勢力很弱 , 讓弱勢力很弱 , 導致弱勢力很弱 , 導致弱勢力很弱 。
since this massive higgs sits along the horizontal direction in this diagram , the photons of electromagnetism remain massless and interact with electric charge along the vertical direction in this charge space .	因為這張圖片中 , 光子的電荷是電荷的主要方向 , 光子是電力的電荷 , 電荷在這個空間中 , 會產生電力的電荷 。
so the electromagnetic and weak forces are described by this pattern of particle charges in twodimensional space .	所以電磁和弱力被稱為二維空間的電磁和弱力 。
we can include the strong force by spreading out its two charge directions and plotting the charges of the force particles in quarks along these directions .	我們能包含強力的力量 , 將它們的兩載載荷 , 將它們的力量分散出來 , 將它們的力量分散出來 , 將它們的力量分散出去 , 將它們的力量分散出去 , 將它們的力量分散出去 。
the charges of all known particles can be plotted in a fourdimensional charge space , and projected down to two dimensions like this so we can see them .	所有的知粒子都可以被放在四維空間中 , 以一個四維空間的基礎組成 , 這樣我們就能看見它們 。
whenever particles interact , nature keeps things in a perfect balance along all four of these charge directions .	當粒子互動時 , 自然保持在完美的平衡上 , 每當粒子互相作用 , 自然會持續在完美的平衡上四分之一 。
if a particle and an antiparticle collide , it creates a burst of energy and a total charge of zero in all four charge directions .	如果粒子和抗粒子 , 它就會產生出能量和一顆粒子 , 它會創造出一顆粒子和抗粒子 , 它會創造出一顆粒子和抗粒子 , 它會創造出一顆粒子和抗粒子 , 它會創造出一顆粒子和抗粒子 。
at this point , anything can be created as long as it has the same energy and maintains a total charge of zero .	在這個時點 , 任何東西都可以被創造出來 , 只要它有同樣的能量和維持一連串的電池 。
for example , this weak force particle and its antiparticle can be created in a collision .	例如 , 這種弱勢力粒子和它的抗粒子可以在一個撞擊中產生 。
in further interactions , the charges must always balance .	在更多的互動中 , 荷爾斯必須總是平衡 。
one of the weak particles could decay into an electron and an antineutrino , and these three still add to zero total charge .	其中一個弱粒子可以分解成電子 , 而這些三個仍然加入了電子和一顆粒子 。
nature always keeps a perfect balance .	大自然總是保持完美的平衡 。
so these patterns of charges are not just pretty .	所以這些圖案並不只是很有趣 。
they tell us what interactions are allowed to happen .	他們告訴我們 , 互動是如何發生的 。
and we can rotate this charge space in four dimensions to get a better look at the strong interaction , which has this nice hexagonal symmetry .	我們能把這個空間帶到四維空間中 , 讓更好的看法更好 , 更好的視力互動 , 讓更好的看法是更好的 。
in a strong interaction , a strong force particle , such as this one , interacts with a colored quark , such as this green one , to give a quark with a different color charge this red one .	在一個強大的力量粒子中 , 例如這個紅色 , 一個強力的粒子 , 例如這個紅色 , 一個強力的粒子 , 例如這個紅色 , 一個強力的粒子 。
and strong interactions are happening millions of times each second in every atom of our bodies , holding the atomic nuclei together .	強大的互動在我們的身體中數百萬次 , 將原子核融合在一起 。
but these four charges corresponding to three forces are not the end of the story .	但這四條曲線對三種力量並不是故事的一部分 。
we can also include two more charges corresponding to the gravitational force .	我們也能包含兩種重力的力量 。
when we include these , each matter particle has two different spin charges , spinup and spindown .	當我們包含這些 , 每個粒子都有兩種不同的旋轉、旋轉和旋轉 。
so they all split , and give a nice pattern in sixdimensional charge space .	所以他們都在六維空間裡做一個很棒的模式
we can rotate this pattern in six dimensions , and see that it's quite pretty .	我們可以在六維空間中移動這個模式 , 看到它很有趣 。
right now , this pattern matches our best current knowledge of how nature is built at the tiny scales of these elementary particles .	現在 , 這個模式將我們最好的知識大自然建立在小規模的大自然中 。
this is what we know for certain .	這就是我們所知道的 。
some of these particles are at the very limit of what we've been able to reach with experiments .	有些粒子是非常限制的 , 我們能夠和實驗進行的實驗 。
from this pattern , we already know the particle physics of these tiny scales . the way the universe works with these tiny scales is very beautiful .	從這個模式中 , 我們已經知道粒子物理是非常美麗的 。
but now i'm going to discuss some new and old ideas about things we don't know yet .	但現在我要討論一些新的和舊的想法 , 關於我們不知道的東西 。
we want to expand this pattern using mathematics alone , and see if we can get our hands on the whole enchilada .	我們想要擴展這個模式使用數學 , 看看我們是否能把手放在整個加州 。
we want to find all the particles and forces that make a complete picture of our universe .	我們想要找到所有粒子和力量 , 讓宇宙的所有粒子和力量 。
and we want to use this picture to predict new particles that we'll see when experiments reach higher energies .	我們想要用這個圖片來預測新的粒子 , 我們希望用這個圖來預測新的粒子 , 以預測新的粒子 。
so there's an old idea in particle physics that this known pattern of charges , which is not very symmetric , could emerge from a more perfect pattern that gets broken similar to how the higgs particle breaks the electroweak pattern to give electromagnetism .	所以 , 在粒子中有一個古老的概念 , 粒子的形狀 , 可以從一個更完美的模式 , 可以從一個更完美的模式 , 可以從一個更完美的模式 , 可以從一個更完美的模式 , 可以從一個更完美的模式 , 可以從一個更完美的模式 , 可以從一個更完美的模式 , 可以從一個更完美的模式 , 可以從一個更完美的模式 , 可以從一個更完美的模式 , 可以從一個更完美的模式 , 可以從更完美的模式 , 可以從一個更完美的模式 , 可以從更完美的模式中 , 可以從更完美的模式中 ,
in order to do this , we need to introduce new forces with new charge directions .	為了做到這一點 , 我們需要介紹新的力量 , 以新方向的新力量 。
when we introduce a new direction , we get to guess what charges the particles have along this direction , and then we can rotate it in with the others .	當我們介紹新方向時 , 我們必須猜測這些粒子在哪裡移動 , 然後我們就能和其他的粒子一起旋轉 。
if we guess wisely , we can construct the standard charges in six charge dimensions as a broken symmetry of this more perfect pattern in seven charge dimensions .	如果我們仔細想想 , 我們就能建構在七維空間之間的標準空間 。
this particular choice corresponds to a grand unified theory introduced by pati and salam in 1973 .	這種特定的選擇在1973年被巴蒂和薩姆斯特定的選擇回應 。
when we look at this new unified pattern , we can see a couple of gaps where particles seem to be missing .	當我們觀察這個新型態度 , 我們可以看到 , 粒子似乎被誤解了 。
this is the way theories of unification work .	這是 「 科學工作 」 的理論
a physicist looks for larger , more symmetric patterns that include the established pattern as a subset .	物理學家看起來更大、更大、更大、更大、更大、更大、更大、更有力的圖形 。
the larger pattern allows us to predict the existence of particles that have never been seen .	更大的模式讓我們能夠預測原始的存在粒子從未見過 。
this unification model predicts the existence of these two new force particles , which should act a lot like the weak force , only weaker .	這種規則的模式預測了這些兩種新力量的存在 , 它應該像弱勢力 , 只有弱勢 。
now we can rotate this set of charges in seven dimensions and consider an odd fact about the matter particles: the second and third generations of matter have exactly the same charges in sixdimensional charge space as the first generation .	現在 , 我們可以把這組合物組成七維空間 , 並考慮一個關於重要的粒子:第二和第三代 , 基本粒子是:第二和第三代 , 基本粒子是:第二和第三代 , 基本粒子是:第二和第三代 。
these particles are not uniquely identified by their six charges .	這些粒子並不獨特地被他們的六個載荷組成 。
they sit on top of one another in the standard charge space .	他們坐在標準中心的空間中 。
however , if we work in eightdimensional charge space , then we can assign unique new charges to each particle .	然而 , 如果在八維空間中 , 我們就可以分辨出獨特的新荷空間 , 可以為每一個粒子組成 。
then we can spin these in eight dimensions , and see what the whole pattern looks like .	接著 , 我們可以用八度維度 , 看看整個模式看起來是什麼樣子 。
here we can see the second and third generations of matter now related to the first generation by a symmetry called " triality . "	在這裡 , 我們可以看到第二和第三代 , 與第一代的相對稱作 「 三世代 」 。
this particular pattern of charges in eight dimensions is actually part of the most beautiful geometric structure in mathematics .	在八維空間中 , 主要是數學中最美妙的幾何結構 。
it's a pattern of the largest exceptional lie group , e8 .	它是最大規模的圖案之一 , 第八個 。
this lie group is a smooth , curved shape with 248 dimensions .	這張圖片是一塊形狀 , 兩個48度的形狀 。
each point in this pattern corresponds to a symmetry of this very complex and beautiful shape .	每個點點都對這個非常複雜且美麗的形狀 。
one small part of this e8 shape can be used to describe the curved spacetime of einstein's general relativity , explaining gravity .	其中一個小小的部分 , 可以用來描述四分之一的曲線 , 解釋重力 。
together with quantum mechanics , the geometry of this shape could describe everything about how the universe works at the tiniest scales .	用量子力學來描述所有關於宇宙如何運作的幾何形狀 。
the pattern of this shape living in eightdimensional charge space is exquisitely beautiful , and it summarizes thousands of possible interactions between these elementary particles , each of which is just a facet of this complicated shape .	這個形狀的形狀在八維空間裡的形狀是非常美麗的 , 每一面都只是一個複雜形狀的形狀 。
as we spin it , we can see many of the other intricate patterns contained in this one .	當我們旋轉時 , 我們可以看到許多其他的圖案在這個過程中 。
and with a particular rotation , we can look down through this pattern in eight dimensions along a symmetry axis and see all the particles at once .	透過這個圖案 , 我們可以看到所有粒子在八度空間中看到所有的粒子 。
it's a very beautiful object , and as with any unification , we can see some holes where new particles are required by this pattern .	這是個非常美麗的物體 , 如同我們所看到的一些洞 , 新的粒子都需要這種模式 。
there are 20 gaps where new particles should be , two of which have been filled by the patisalam particles .	新粒子有20個差距 , 新粒子都被稱為 「 粒子 」 的粒子 。
from their location in this pattern , we know that these new particles should be scalar fields like the higgs particle , but have color charge and interact with the strong force .	在這個圖案中 , 我們知道這些新粒子會像希格斯粒子 , 但有顏色和強力 。
filling in these new particles completes this pattern , giving us the full e8 .	在這些新的粒子中 , 把這些新粒子變成了這個模式 , 給予我們全部的8 。
this e8 pattern has very deep mathematical roots .	這八種模式有非常深的數學根源 。
it's considered by many to be the most beautiful structure in mathematics .	它被認為是數學中最美麗的結構 。
it's a fantastic prospect that this object of great mathematical beauty could describe the truth of particle interactions at the smallest scales imaginable .	這是個很棒的數學美麗 , 可以描述真相對於粒子互動的真相 , 很棒的數學美麗可以描述真實的粒子相互作用 。
and this idea that nature is described by mathematics is not at all new .	大自然的概念是 , 大自然被數學並非全新的 。
in 1623 , galileo wrote this: " nature's grand book , which stands continually open to our gaze , is written in the language of mathematics .	在1623年 , 《大自然雜誌》寫了一篇文章 , 寫了: 「 大自然的本書 , 用數學的角度來描述它 。
its characters are triangles , circles and other geometrical figures , without which it is humanly impossible to understand a single word of it ; without these , one is wandering around in a dark labyrinth . "	角色是三角形、圓形、圓形、圓形、圓形、圓形、圓形和其他幾何形狀 , 不論是哪一個人都無法理解一個單字 , 不論是誰 , 都無法理解一句話 , 不論是誰 , 都無法理解一句話 , 不論是誰 , 都無法理解一個單詞 。
i believe this to be true , and i've tried to follow galileo's guidance in describing the mathematics of particle physics using only triangles , circles and other geometrical figures .	我相信這是真的 , 我相信這真的是真的 , 我一直嘗試遵伽伽利略的數學粒子物理學用只有三角形、圓形和其他幾何形狀 。
of course , when other physicists and i actually work on this stuff , the mathematics can resemble a dark labyrinth .	當然 , 身為物理學家 , 我真的在研究這些東西 , 數學可以組成一個黑暗的實驗室 。
but it's reassuring that at the heart of this mathematics is pure , beautiful geometry .	但這數學的數學是純粹、美麗的幾何形狀 。
joined with quantum mechanics , this mathematics describes our universe as a growing e8 coral , with particles interacting at every location in all possible ways according to a beautiful pattern .	與量子力學有關 , 這個數學描述了我們的宇宙 , 以一種美麗的形式呈現出一個美麗的形狀 。
and as more of the pattern comes into view using new machines like the large hadron collider , we may be able to see whether nature uses this e8 pattern or a different one .	隨著更多的新機器 , 我們可能可以看到大型的大型鐵粒 , 我們可能可以看出自然使用新機器 , 像大型鐵粒一樣 , 我們可能可以看見自然使用新的機器 , 像大型鐵子一樣 。
this process of discovery is a wonderful adventure to be involved in .	這個過程發現的是一個很棒的冒險 。
if the lhc finds particles that fit this e8 pattern , that will be very , very cool .	如果lhc找到粒子 , 它會很酷 。
if the lhc finds new particles , but they don't fit this pattern well , that will be very interesting , but bad for this e8 theory .	如果lhc找到新的粒子 , 但它們不適合這個模式 , 那會很有趣 , 但不用這種模式 , 那會很有趣 , 但卻不適合這個模式 。

now how bad would that be ?	那麼 , 多麼糟糕 ?
well , pretty bad .	嗯 , 很糟糕 。
but predicting how nature works is a very risky game .	但預測大自然的運作是非常危險的遊戲 。
this theory and others like it are long shots .	這種理論和其他類似的東西是很長的 。
one does a lot of hard work knowing that most of these ideas probably won't end up being true about nature .	很多人都知道 , 大部分這些想法可能不會結束對自然的影響 。
that's what doing theoretical physics is like: there are a lot of wipeouts .	這就是理論物理學的理論物理就像:有許多野生 。
in this regard , new physics theories are a lot like startup companies .	在這個區域 , 新物理理論就像創創公司一樣 。
as with any large investment , it can be emotionally difficult to abandon a line of research when it isn't working out .	只要有任何大型投資 , 就會很困難 , 不用在工作時 , 會很困難 。

now , the only way to maintain sanity and achieve happiness in the midst of this uncertainty is to keep balance and perspective in life .	唯一能維持保持平衡和觀點就是保持平衡和觀點 。
i've tried the best i can to live a balanced life .	我曾嘗試過最好的辦法 , 能活得平衡的生活 。
i try to balance my life equally between physics , love and surfing my own three charge directions .	我試著平衡我自己的三條路徑 。

and you can tell an awful lot about what those beings looked like from the fossils , from the shape of the muscle attachments , something about the way they lived from the various artifacts found with them .	你可以告訴大家很多關於這些東西的樣子 , 像是來自化石 , 來自化石的形狀 , 和它們的形狀 , 來自化石的形狀 , 和它們的形狀 。
but what about how they behaved ? that's what he wanted to know .	但他們怎麼做呢 ? 這就是他想要知道的 。
and of course , behavior doesn't fossilize .	當然 , 行為不會化化 。
he argued and it's now a fairly common theory that if we found behavior patterns similar or the same in our closest living relatives , the great apes , and humans today , then maybe those behaviors were present in the apelike , humanlike ancestor some seven million years ago .	他說 , 很常見的理論是 , 如果我們找到行為模式或相同的行為模式 , 如同我們最親近的親戚 , 人類的祖先 , 或許這些行為模式和人類一樣 , 大約七百萬年前 , 這種行為模式相似或相同 。
and therefore , perhaps we had brought those characteristics with us from that ancient , ancient past .	因此 , 也許我們從古老、古老、古老的歷史上 , 已經帶出了這些特徵 。
well , if you look in textbooks today that deal with human evolution , you very often find people speculating about how early humans may have behaved , based on the behavior of chimpanzees .	嗯 , 如果你看看現今的教科書 , 人類進化 , 你通常會發現人類演化的行為 , 通常會發現人類演化的行為 , 通常會發現人類演化的行為 。
they are more like us than any other living creature , and we've heard about that during this ted conference .	牠們比其他生物還多 , 我們也聽過在ted會議中 。
so it remains for me to comment on the ways in which chimpanzees are so like us , in certain aspects of their behavior .	所以 , 為了我來評估這些黑猩猩的行為 , 我們的行為是如此的 。
every chimpanzee has his or her own personality .	每個黑猩猩都有自己的個人性 。
of course , i gave them names . they can live to be 60 years or more , although we think most of them probably don't make it to 60 in the wild .	當然 , 我給了他們名字 , 他們可以活到60歲 , 儘管我們認為大多數人可能不會在野外生存60歲 。
mr . wurzel . the female has her first baby when she's 11 or 12 .	mr.wurzel.wurzel是第一個嬰兒在11或12歲的時候
thereafter , she has one baby only every five or six years , a long period of childhood dependency when the child is nursing , sleeping with the mother at night , and riding on her back .	在那裡 , 她有一個嬰兒 , 每五歲或六年 , 每五歲或六年都很長一段時間 , 孩子們在睡眠時 , 媽媽在晚上睡覺 , 和母親一起睡著 , 把她帶回來 。
and we believe that this long period of childhood is important for chimpanzees , just as it is for us , in relation to learning .	我們相信 , 對於黑猩猩來說 , 對於黑猩猩來說 , 對於黑猩猩來說 , 對於黑猩猩來說 , 我們相信這個長期對黑猩猩來說是很重要的 , 只要我們和學習有關 。
as the brain becomes ever more complex during evolution in different forms of animals , so we find that learning plays an ever more important role in an individual's life history .	隨著大腦變得更複雜 , 所以 , 我們發現學習扮演了重要的角色 , 以不同類型動物的角度來看 , 我們發現學習扮演了重要的角色 。
and young chimpanzees spend a lot of time watching what their elders do .	年輕的黑猩猩花了很多時間觀察牠們的生長 。
we know now that they're capable of imitating behaviors that they see .	我們現在知道 , 牠們有能力模仿牠們的行為 。
and we believe that it's in this way that the different toolusing behaviors that have now been seen in all the different chimpanzee populations studied in africa how these are passed from one generation to the next , through observation , imitation and practice , so that we can describe these toolusing behaviors as primitive culture .	我們相信 , 透過觀察、限制和練習 , 我們相信 , 透過觀察、限制和練習的行為 , 我們就能描述這些虛構的行為 , 透過觀察、限制 , 和練習 , 讓我們能夠描述這些虛構的行為 。
chimpanzees don't have a spoken language . we've talked about that .	黑猩猩沒有一種語言 , 我們已經談到這一點 。
they do have a very rich repertoire of postures and gestures , many of which are similar , or even identical , to ours and formed in the same context . greeting chimpanzees embracing .	他們的確有非常豐富的豐富的皮膚 , 甚至是相似的 , 或甚至身分在同一個情境中 , 許多人都相似 , 或甚至身分在同一個情境中 。
they also kiss , hold hands , pat one another on the back .	它們也吻合 , 雙手 , 手上 , 把手放在回來 。
and they swagger and they throw rocks .	然後他們會搖滾 。
in chimpanzee society , we find many , many examples of compassion , precursors to love and true altruism .	在黑猩猩社會中 , 我們發現很多很多的例子 , 包括同情心、喜愛和真實的利潤 。
unfortunately , they , like us , have a dark side to their nature .	不幸的是 , 它們就像我們一樣 , 牠們的大自然 。
they're capable of extreme brutality , even a kind of primitive war .	它們是極端殘酷的 , 甚至是極端的殘酷 。
and these really aggressive behaviors , for the most part , are directed against individuals of the neighboring social group .	這些真正的侵略性行為 , 大部分的部分 , 都被反對鄰居社區群體的行為 。
they are very territorially aggressive .	它們是非常精彩的動作 。
chimpanzees , i believe , more than any other living creature , have helped us to understand that , after all , there is no sharp line between humans and the rest of the animal kingdom .	黑猩猩 , 我相信 , 比任何其他生物都能幫助我們了解 , 人類和動物王國之間沒有鯊魚 。
it's a very blurry line , and it's getting more blurry all the time as we make even more observations .	它是非常模糊的 , 每當我們做更多的觀察 , 就會變得更加緊張 。
the study that i began in 1960 is still continuing to this day .	我在1960年開始的研究 , 那時我開始在1960年仍然持續 。
and these chimpanzees , living their complex social lives in the wild , have helped more than anything else to make us realize we are part of , and not separated from , the amazing animals with whom we share the planet .	這些黑猩猩 , 在野生動物中 , 牠們的複雜社群生活在野外 , 牠們的複雜社群生活在野外 , 讓我們了解到 , 沒有分離 , 和我們共享的地球 。
so it's pretty sad to find that chimpanzees , like so many other creatures around the world , are losing their habitats .	所以 , 令人驚訝的是 , 發現黑猩猩 , 像世界上許多其他生物一樣 , 牠們的棲息地都失去了棲息地 。

and it was when i flew over the whole area , about 16 years ago , and realized that outside the park , this forest , which in 1960 had stretched almost unbroken along the eastern shore of lake tanganyika , which is where the tiny , 30squaremile gombe national park lies , that a question came to my mind .	當時我在1960年時期 , 發現在公園裡 , 當時我在公園裡 , 發現在公園之外 , 在1960年以前 , 幾乎沒有破壞的土地 , 大約16年前 , 當時在公園裡 , 一個問題來到我的腦海裡 。
" how can we even try to save these famous chimpanzees , when the people living around the national park are struggling to survive ? "	「 我們要如何嘗試拯救這些有名的黑猩猩 , 當人們住在國家公園時 , 那些有名的黑猩猩 ? 」
more people are living there than the land could possibly support .	更多的人住在土地上 , 無法支持 。
the numbers increased by refugees pouring in from burundi and over the lake from congo .	數量的增加 , 來自布朗克斯的數量增加 。
and very poor people they couldn't afford to buy food from elsewhere .	很窮的人 , 他們無法負擔得買食物 。
this led to a program , which we call tacare .	我們稱之為 「 tacare 」 。
it's a very holistic way of improving the lives of the people living in the villages around the park .	這是一種非常可愛的方式 , 讓人們住在公園裡的生活方式 。
it started small with 12 villages . it's now in 24 .	它從12個村莊開始小 , 現在是24歲 。
there isn't time to go into it , but it's including things like tree nurseries , methods of farming most suitable to this now very degraded , almost desertlike land up in these mountains .	沒有時間去進去 , 但它包括像樹木護士 , 幾乎沙漠的土地在這些山上 。
ways of controlling , preventing soil erosion .	控制 , 防止土壤消耗 。
ways of reclaiming overused farmland , so that within two years they can again be productive .	重建農島的土地 , 兩年後 , 牠們可以再次生產力 。
working to help the villagers obtain fresh water from wells .	為了幫助那些村民從水中獲取水 。
perhaps build some schoolrooms .	或許建造一些學校 。
most important of all , i believe , is working with small groups of women , providing them with opportunities for microcredit loans .	最重要的是 , 我相信 , 和小群婦女合作 , 提供他們機會 , 提供給微型貸款的機會 。
and we've got , as is the case around the world , about 95 percent of all loans returned .	我們已經發現了 , 全球的百分之九十五的貸款都回來了 。
empowering women , working with education , providing scholarships for girls so they can finish secondary school , in the clear understanding that , all around the world , as women's education improves , family size drops .	賦予女性的教育 , 提供獎學金給女孩們 , 讓她們能夠完成第二課 , 讓女性教育改善 , 家庭大小的成績 。
we provide information about family planning and about hiv/aids .	我們提供資訊關於家庭計畫和愛滋病的資訊 。
and as a result of this program , something's happening for conservation .	為了保育這個計畫的結果 , 一切都在保育 。

were they interested in conservation ? absolutely not .	他們對保育有興趣嗎 ? 絕對不是 。
they were interested in health ; they were interested in education .	他們對健康有興趣 , 他們對教育有興趣 。
and as time went on , and as their situation began to improve , they began to understand ever more about the need for conservation .	隨著時間 , 當他們開始改善 , 他們開始了解更多關於保育的需求 。
they began to understand that as the upper levels of the hills were denuded of trees , so you've got this terrible soil erosion and mudslides .	他們開始了解到 , 海岸的大樓層面是樹木 , 所以你有了非常可怕的石油和泥土 。

and when you get large numbers of people living in land that is not that fertile , particularly when you cut down trees , and you leave the soil open to the wind for erosion , as desperate populations cut down more and more trees , so that they can try and grow food for themselves and their families , what's going to happen ? something's got to give .	當你把土壤放到海岸 , 特別是當你砍伐樹木時 , 會發生什麼事 ? 什麼會發生什麼事 ? 什麼事會發生 ? 什麼事會發生 ?

the indigenous people around the world , before they made a major decision , used to sit around and ask themselves , " how does this decision affect our people seven generations ahead ? "	世界各地的人都在問自己: 「 這個決定如何影響我們的人民七代前進 ? 」

"	今天 , 主要的決策 , 不是特別談論非洲 , 但開發中國家最主要的決策 , 包括數百萬人 , 通常是基於: 「 這會如何影響下一百萬人的觀點 ? 」

as i began traveling around africa talking about the problems faced by chimpanzees and their vanishing forests , i realized more and more how so many of africa's problems could be laid at the door of previous colonial exploitation .	當我開始在非洲各地討論這些問題時 , 我了解到更多 , 很多非洲的問題 , 會被黑猩猩和他們的優勢森林砍伐 , 我發現更多 , 很多非洲的問題 , 會被黑猩猩和他們的優勢森林 , 我了解到更多 , 很多非洲的問題 , 會被黑猩猩和他們的優勢森林砍伐 。

the water water is perhaps one of the most crucial issues that we're going to face in this century and everywhere water is being polluted by agricultural , industrial and household chemicals that still are being sprayed around the world , seemingly with the inability to profit from past experience .	水水水可能是最關鍵的問題之一 , 我們在這個世紀中所看到的 , 包括農業、工業、工業和家庭化學物質 , 還在世界各地被農業、工業及家庭化的化學物質 , 幾乎都能從過去經驗中獲取 。
the mangroves are being cut down ; the effects of things like the tsunami get worse .	紅外線的效果就像海嘯更糟糕 。

we have the reckless burning of fossil fuels along with other greenhouse gasses , so called , leading to climate change .	我們有無可避免的燃料和其他溫室氣體 , 所以稱之為氣候變遷 。
finally , all around the world , people have begun to believe that there is something going on very wrong with our climate .	最後 , 在世界各地 , 大家都相信 , 我們的氣候變遷有很大的影響 。
all around the world climates are mixed up .	全世界的氣候都被混合起來了 。
and it's the poor people who are affected worse .	貧窮的人會影響更糟糕 。
it's africa that already is affected .	非洲已經被影響了 。
in many parts of subsaharan africa , the droughts are so much worse .	在撒哈拉南非洲的許多地區 , 乾旱更糟糕 。
and when the rain does come , it so often leads to flooding and added distress , and the cycle of poverty and hunger and disease .	當雨季發生時 , 通常會導致災難、飢餓、飢餓和疾病的循環 。
and the numbers of people living in an area that the land cannot support , who are too poor to buy food , who can't move away because the whole land is degraded .	住在一個地區的地區 , 人們住在一個地區 , 沒有辦法離開 , 因為整個陸地都被降低了 。
and so you get desertification creeping , creeping , creeping as the last of the trees are cut down .	所以你會被切割下來 , 再回顧 , 回覆 , 回覆 , 最後一棵樹就被砍掉了 。

well , do you think there could be some kind of disconnect between this extraordinarily clever brain , the kind of brain that the ted technologies exemplify , and the human heart ? talking about it in the nonscientific term , in terms of love and compassion . is there some disconnect ?	嗯 , 你認為有一些不同意見的大腦 , 與同情心有關嗎 ? 關於愛和同情心 , 不論是哪些人的腦袋 ? 和同情心有關嗎 ? 關於愛和同情心 , 沒有人心 ?
and these young people , when i talk to them , basically they were either depressed or apathetic , or bitter and angry . and they said more or less the same thing , " we feel this way because we feel you've compromised our future and there's nothing we can do about it . "	這些年輕人 , 當我和他們談話時 , 他們說的 , 不論是不一樣的 , 基本上 , 他們會說: 「 我們感覺到 , 因為我們覺得你對我們有所貢獻 , 不論他們是誰 , 不論是誰 , 或同儕 , 或同一件事 , 我們感覺到他們 , 基本上他們也沒有什麼能做的事 。 」

artist dianna cohen shares some tough truths about plastic pollution in the ocean and in our lives and some thoughts on how to free ourselves from the plastic gyre .	藝術家diannacohen分享了一些關於塑膠污染的真相 , 關於塑膠污染的真相 , 在我們的生活中 , 和一些關於塑膠污染的真相 。
consumerism , global issues , green , mission blue , oceans , plastic	消費主義、全球議題、綠色、藍色、海洋、塑膠 。
dianna cohen: tough truths about plastic pollution	狄安娜•柯林:對塑膠污染的真相 。
i'm a visual artist , and i'm also one of the cofounders of the plastic pollution coalition .	我是個視覺藝術家 , 我也是其中一位視覺藝術家 , 我也是一種塑膠污染中心的共同創作 。
i've been working with plastic bags , which i cut up and sew back together as my primary material for my artwork for the last 20 years .	我和塑膠袋一起工作 , 把我帶到過去二十年來 , 用塑膠袋來做 。
i turn them into two and threedimensional pieces and sculptures and installations .	我把它們轉換成兩個、雕塑和雕塑 。
upon working with the plastic , after about the first eight years , some of my work started to fissure and break down into smaller little bits of plastic .	過去八年來 , 我的工作開始把焦點放入小小的塑膠中 。
and i thought , " great .	我心想: 「 很棒 。
it's ephemeral just like us . "	像我們一樣 。 」
upon educating myself a little further about plastics , i actually realized this was a bad thing .	隨著塑膠 , 我意識到這是個壞事 。
it's a bad thing that plastic breaks down into smaller little bits , because it's always still plastic .	塑膠碎片很糟 , 因為它總是仍然塑膠 。
and what we're finding is that a lot of it is in the marine environment .	我們發現 , 在海洋環境中 , 許多人都在海洋環境中 。
i then , in the last few years , learned about the pacific garbage patch and the gyre .	在過去幾年 , 我發現了太平洋的垃圾和gy 。
and my initial reaction and i think this is a lot of people's first reaction to learning about it is , " oh my god !	而我的第一個反應是 , 我認為這是很多人的第一反應 , 就是: 「 喔 ! 我的天啊 !

phyllis rodriguez and aicha elwafi have a powerful friendship born of unthinkable loss . rodriguez' son was killed in the world trade center attacks on september 11 , 2001 ; elwafi's son zacarias moussaoui was convicted of a role in those attacks and is serving a life sentence . in hoping to find peace , these two moms have come to understand and respect one another .	菲利斯•羅德里德瑞茲和平德瑞茲在2001年9月11日 , 2001年9月11日 , 2001年9月11日 , 阿爾瓦菲•羅德里德里斯和平 , 這兩隻媽媽都來找和平 , 這兩隻媽媽都來找和平 , 這些兩隻媽媽都來找和平 , 這兩隻媽媽都來了解和平 。

before lifesaver , the best hand filters were only capable of filtering down to about 200 nanometers .	在生命saver之前 , 最好的手濾器只能在200奈米尺度下降到200奈米 。
the smallest bacteria is about 200 nanometers .	最小的細菌是200奈米 。
so a 200nanometer bacteria is going to get through a 200nanometer hole .	所以 , 一個200奈米的細菌會從200奈米的細菌開始 。
the smallest virus , on the other hand , is about 25 nanometers .	最小的病毒是大約25奈米 。
so that's definitely going to get through those 200 nanometer holes .	所以 , 這絕對是從200奈米的角度來看 。
lifesaver pores are 15 nanometers .	生活品質是15奈米 。
so nothing is getting through .	沒什麼事發生 。

so , by thinking differently , and processing water at the point of use , mothers and children no longer have to walk four hours a day to collect their water .	所以 , 想想看 , 母親和孩子們不再需要走四小時 , 去收集他們的水 。

now notice , in a period which is dominated by a monopolar world , you have fixed alliances nato , the warsaw pact .	注意到 , 在日常生活中 , 由一個微小的二氧化碳組成 , 你已經填補了所有人 , 以致於 「 天空 」 的 「 日子 」 。

you get swine flu in mexico , it's a problem for charles de gaulle airport 24 hours later .	你在墨西哥的氣候變遷 , 都在墨西哥 , 這是一個問題 , 在墨西哥 , 它是個問題在墨西哥灣 , 它是個問題在墨西哥灣 , 花了24小時後 。
lehman brothers goes down , the whole lot collapses .	雷德曼兄弟會下降 , 整個大爆炸 。

and what that means is the idea of a nation state acting alone , not connected with others , not working with others , is no longer a viable proposition .	意思是 , 國家和其他人的關係 , 沒有與其他人合作 , 而不是與其他人合作 , 而不是與其他人合作 , 而不是與其他人合作 , 而不是與其他人合作 。
because the actions of a nation state are neither confined to itself , nor is it sufficient for the nation state itself to control its own territory , because the effects outside the nation state are now beginning to affect what happens inside them .	因為聯合國政府的權力不足 , 因為美國國家的效果會影響到國家本身 , 讓國家本身無法控制它本身 , 因為在國內的效果 , 國家本身也沒有效率 , 因為對國家國家的影響會發生在他們身上 。
i was a young soldier in the last of the small empire wars of britain .	我是一位年輕士兵 , 當時是英國的年輕士兵 。
at that time , the defense of my country was about one thing and one thing only: how strong was our army , how strong was our air force , how strong was our navy and how strong were our allies .	那時 , 我國家的軍隊有多強 , 我們的軍隊 , 我們的軍隊 , 有強大的力量 , 我們的軍隊 , 我們的軍隊 , 強大的力量 , 我們的軍隊 , 我們的軍隊 , 我們的軍隊有多強大 , 我們的軍隊有強大的力量 。
that was when the enemy was outside the walls .	當敵人在牆壁時 , 敵人是外牆 。

now if i want to talk about the defense of my country , i have to speak to the minister of health because pandemic disease is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of agriculture because food security is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of industry because the fragility of our hitech infrastructure is now a point of attack for our enemies as we see from cyber warfare i have to speak to the minister of home affairs because who has entered my country , who lives in that terraced house in that inner city has a direct effect on what happens in my country as we in london saw in the 7/7 bombings .	現在 , 如果我想要談談我的國家 , 我必須談談我的國家 , 我必須談談我的國家 , 我必須談談防護 , 我必須談談防護 , 我必須談談防護 , 我必須談談防禦 , 我必須談到我的國家 , 對於我的國家來說 , 我得談談防禦 , 我必須談到我的國家 , 對於我的國家來說 , 要談談防禦 , 我必須談到我的國家 , 對於我的國家來說 , 要談談防禦 , 我必須談到我的國家 , 對於我的國家來說 , 要談談防禦 , 我必須談到我的國家 , 對於我的國家來說 , 要談到我的國家 , 我必須談談防禦 , 我必須談到我的國家 , 對於我的國家 , 對於安全 , 我必須對抗爭議 , 要談談我的國家 , 我必須談談防禦 , 我必須對抗議 , 要談談我的國家 , 要談談防禦 , 我必須談談防禦 , 我必須和國內的抗爭者談談 , 我得要談談防禦 , 我必須談到我的國家 , 對於我的國家 , 要談到我的國家 , 我得要談談防禦 ,
it's no longer the case that the security of a country is simply a matter for its soldiers and its ministry of defense .	它不再是美國國家的安全性 , 一個國家的安全只是一個國家的安全 , 一個國家的安全是很重要的 。
it's its capacity to lock together its institutions .	它的能力可以鎖組成立體制 。
and this tells you something very important .	這告訴你一件很重要的事 。
it tells you that , in fact , our governments , vertically constructed , constructed on the economic model of the industrial revolution vertical hierarchy , specialization of tasks , command structures have got the wrong structures completely .	它告訴各位 , 事實上 , 我們的政府 , 在工業革命的經濟模式上 , 建構在工業革命的經濟模型上 , 建構在工業革命的經濟模型 , 實際上 , 政府 , 基本上 , 建構在工業革命的經濟模型 , 實際上 , 政府 , 基本上 , 建構在工業革命的經濟模型 。
you in business know that the paradigm structure of our time , ladies and gentlemen , is the network .	你在商業知道 , 我們的典型結構 , 是網路 。
it's your capacity to network that matters , both within your governments and externally .	它是你的權力 , 在你的政府和外面 , 都在你的政府和外面 。
so here is ashdown's third law .	這是三條法律 。
by the way , don't ask me about ashdown's first law and second law because i haven't invented those yet ; it always sounds better if there's a third law , doesn't it ?	順道一提 , 如果有第三條法律 , 不要問我第一個法律和第二個法律 , 因為我沒有發明 , 不問我是否有第三條法律 , 不是嗎 ?
ashdown's third law is that in the modern age , where everything is connected to everything , the most important thing about what you can do is what you can do with others .	第三條法則是 , 在現代時代 , 所有事物都連結在一起 , 最重要的事情是你能做什麼和其他人有關 。
the most important bit about your structure whether you're a government , whether you're an army regiment , whether you're a business is your docking points , your interconnectors , your capacity to network with others .	最重要的一點是你是政府 , 無論你是企業 , 無論你是政府 , 無論你是企業 , 你的權力 , 無論你是企業 , 你的權力 , 無論你是企業 , 你的權力 , 無論你是企業 , 你的權力 , 無論你是企業 , 你的權力 , 無論你是企業 , 你的權力 ,
