if it is the case , ladies and gentlemen and it is that we are now locked together in a way that has never been quite the same before , then it's also the case that we share a destiny with each other .	假如 , 女士們先生們 , 我們現在與彼此之間的聯繫在一起 , 這也是我們與彼此相同的案例 。
suddenly and for the very first time , collective defense , the thing that has dominated us as the concept of securing our nations , is no longer enough .	突然間 , 首次 , 集體防禦 , 已經把我們視為 「 不夠 」 的概念 , 將我們視為 「 不夠 」 的概念 。
it used to be the case that if my tribe was more powerful than their tribe , i was safe ; if my country was more powerful than their country , i was safe ; my alliance , like nato , was more powerful than their alliance , i was safe .	一般來說 , 我是安全的 , 如果我的國家比他們的國家更強大 , 我是安全的 , 如果我的國家比他們的國家更強大 , 我是安全的 , 我是安全的 。
it is no longer the case .	它不再是這樣 。
the advent of the interconnectedness and of the weapons of mass destruction means that , increasingly , i share a destiny with my enemy .	聯合國與敵人之間的關係 , 與敵人之間的聯繫 , 與敵人之間的聯繫 。
when i was a diplomat negotiating the disarmament treaties with the soviet union in geneva in the 1970s , we succeeded because we understood we shared a destiny with them .	當我在1970年代 , 我們成功了 , 我們成功了因為我們了解了我們與他們共享的特定 。
collective security is not enough .	集體安全並不足夠 。
peace has come to northern ireland because both sides realized that the zerosum game couldn't work .	和平也來到北極洲 , 因為兩邊都意識到 , 和平 , 因為兩邊都意識到 , 和平都無法運作 。
they shared a destiny with their enemies .	他們和敵人一起共享 。
one of the great barriers to peace in the middle east is that both sides , both israel and , i think , the palestinians , do not understand that they share a collective destiny .	在中東地區最棒的障礙之一 , 就是兩邊 , 兩邊 , 巴勒斯坦人 , 不了解他們共享集體的一面 。
and so suddenly , ladies and gentlemen , what has been the proposition of visionaries and poets down the ages becomes something we have to take seriously as a matter of public policy .	突然間 , 女士們先生們 , 女士們先生們 , 我們必須認同一個公共政策的重要性 。
i started with a poem , i'll end with one .	我從一首詩開始 , 我會結束 。
the great poem of john donne's .	約翰•唐尼的偉大詩 。
" send not for whom the bell tolls . "	「 不要把貝殼賣出來 。 」
the poem is called " no man is an island . "	這首詩叫做 「 沒有人是島嶼 」
and it goes: " every man's death affected me , for i am involved in mankind , send not to ask for whom the bell tolls , it tolls for thee . "	然後他們說: 「 每個人的死亡都會影響我 , 每人死亡都會影響我 , 每人死亡都影響我 , 對我來說 , 每個人的死亡都會影響我 。 」
for john donne , a recommendation of morality .	約翰•唐納所說的 , 是道德的建議 。
for us , i think , part of the equation for our survival .	對我們來說 , 我認為 , 其中一部分是為了我們的生存 。
to find the path to long life and health , dan buettner and team study the world's " blue zones , " communities whose elders live with vim and vigor to recordsetting age . at tedxtc , he shares the 9 common diet and lifestyle habits that keep them spry past age 100 .	為了找到一條路徑 , 長壽命和健康 , 丹佛頓和世界的 「 藍色區 」 , 在那裡 , 他分享了9個共同的飲食和生活方式 , 來記錄年齡 , 在tedxttner和團隊研究世界的 「 藍色區塊 」 , 每一百歲的人都住在tedxtner 。
biology , culture , exploration , food , health , life , science	生物學、文化、探索、食物、健康、生命、科學 。
dan buettner: how to live to be 100+	danbuetner:如何活到100+
something called the danish twin study established that only about 10 percent of how long the average person lives , within certain biological limits , is dictated by our genes .	一個叫做dandndnishtwin研究的發現 , 只需要10%的壽命 , 只有10%的長壽命 , 人類生活在某些生物限制中 , 我們的基因會被遺傳 。
the other 90 percent is dictated by our lifestyle .	其他90%被我們的生活方式分解 。
so the premise of blue zones: if we can find the optimal lifestyle of longevity we can come up with a de facto formula for longevity .	所以 , 藍色區塊:如果我們能找到最佳的生命形式 , 我們能找到最佳的生命形式 , 以長壽的方式來分析 。
but if you ask the average american what the optimal formula of longevity is , they probably couldn't tell you .	但如果你問一般美國人的平均壽命 , 他們可能無法告訴你 。
they've probably heard of the south beach diet , or the atkins diet .	他們可能聽過南海灘飲食 , 或是皮膚飲食 。
you have the usda food pyramid .	你有美國食物金字塔 。
there is what oprah tells us .	歐普拉告訴我們 。
there is what doctor oz tells us .	醫生奧茲告訴我們 。
the fact of the matter is there is a lot of confusion around what really helps us live longer better .	重點是 , 有很多混亂 , 讓我們更好更好 。
should you be running marathons or doing yoga ?	你應該要跑馬拉松或做瑜伽嗎 ?
should you eat organic meats or should you be eating tofu ?	應該要吃掉毒肉 , 或應該吃肉 ?
when it comes to supplements , should you be taking them ?	當它到供應時 , 應該要帶他們嗎 ?
how about these hormones or resveratrol ?	這些荷爾蒙或逆轉性呢 ?
and does purpose play into it ?	目的是嗎 ?
spirituality ? and how about how we socialize ?	精神性 ? 我們如何社會化 ?
well , our approach to finding longevity was to team up with national geographic , and the national institute on aging , to find the four demographically confirmed areas that are geographically defined .	嗯 , 我們的國家地理協調 , 找到了國家地理協定 , 和國家地理協定 , 和國家地理協定 , 和國家地理協定 , 和國家地理協定 , 和國家地理協定 , 找到四分之一的國家地理 。
and then bring a team of experts in there to methodically go through exactly what these people do , to distill down the crosscultural distillation .	接著 , 把各式各樣的專家們帶進去 , 去了解這些人做的事 , 把專家的專家們帶進去 , 去了解這些人做的事 , 將跨越文化的分裂 。
and at the end of this i'm going to tell you what that distillation is .	最後我要告訴各位 , 發生了什麼事 。
but first i'd like to debunk some common myths when it comes to longevity .	但首先 , 我想要解開一些常見的迷思 , 來延長壽命 。
and the first myth is if you try really hard you can live to be 100 .	第一個謎題是:如果你嘗試真的很難可以活到100歲 。
the problem is , only about one out of 5 , 000 people in america live to be 100 .	問題是 , 只有一萬五千人在美國生活中只有一百人 。
your chances are very low .	你的機會非常低 。
even though it's the fastest growing demographic in america , it's hard to reach 100 .	即使是美國最快的人口數量 , 很難達到100 。
the problem is that we're not programmed for longevity .	問題是 , 我們不是為了長壽而來的 。
we are programmed for something called procreative success .	我們被稱為 「 成功 」 的成功 。
i love that word .	我喜歡這個詞 。
it reminds me of my college days .	它提醒了我大學的日子 。
biologists term procreative success to mean the age where you have children and then another generation , the age when your children have children .	生物學家說 , 年齡是孩子的年齡 , 當你的孩子有孩子時 , 你的孩子有孩子的年齡 。
after that the effect of evolution completely dissipates .	經過演化的影響之後 , 演化完全消失了 。
if you're a mammal , if you're a rat or an elephant , or a human , in between , it's the same story .	如果你是哺乳動物 , 如果你是哺乳動物 , 或人類 , 或一個人 , 相同的故事 。
so to make it to age 100 , you not only have to have had a very good lifestyle , you also have to have won the genetic lottery .	為了讓它到達100歲 , 你不只需要有非常好的生活方式 , 你也必須有非常好的生活方式 , 你也必須有好的生活方式 。
the second myth is , there are treatments that can help slow , reverse , or even stop aging .	第二個迷思是 , 治療能協助緩慢、反轉 , 或甚至停止 。
when you think of it , there is 99 things that can age us .	當你想到它時 , 我們有99個東西可以用我們 。
deprive your brain of oxygen for just a few minutes , those brain cells die , they never come back .	把你的腦細胞死掉 , 那些腦細胞死亡 , 他們從來沒有回來 。
play tennis too hard , on your knees , ruin your cartilage , the cartilage never comes back .	玩耍太硬了 , 你的膝蓋 , 車子不會回來 。
our arteries can clog . our brains can gunk up with plaque , and we can get alzheimer's .	我們的藝術家可以克服 , 我們的腦袋可以穿梭 , 我們的腦袋可以停止 , 我們的腦袋可以穿上去 , 我們的腦袋可以穿上衣服 , 我們的大腦可以穿上衣服 。
there is just too many things to go wrong .	很多事情都錯了 。
our bodies have 35 trillion cells , trillion with a " t . " we're talking national debt numbers here .	我們的身體有35兆個細胞 , 叫做 「 t 」 , 我們在說國家債務 。
those cells turn themselves over once every eight years .	每八年來 , 這種細胞就會自動一次 。
and every time they turn themselves over there is some damage . and that damage builds up .	每當他們把自己丟到一個損傷後 , 會造成傷害 , 造成傷害 。
and it builds up exponentially .	它建構了大量的設計 。
it's a little bit like the days when we all had beatles albums or eagles albums and we'd make a copy of that on a cassette tape , and let our friends copy that cassette tape , and pretty soon , with successive generations that tape sounds like garbage .	這有點像是垃圾 , 我們有一群小小的代碼 , 像是垃圾 , 讓朋友們複製 , 很快地 , 讓朋友複製 , 很快地 , 讓朋友複製 , 很快地 , 讓朋友複製 , 很快地 , 讓朋友複製 , 很快就有成功的代碼 。
well , the same things happen to our cells .	同樣的事發生在我們的細胞身上 。
that's why a 65yearold person is aging at a rate of about 125 times faster than a 12yearold person .	這是為什麼65倍的速度比十二歲的人還快 。
so , if there is nothing you can do to slow your aging or stop your aging , what am i doing here ?	所以 , 如果有沒有任何東西可以減緩或停止你 , 我在做什麼 ?
well , the fact of the matter is the best science tells us that the capacity of the human body , my body , your body , is about 90 years , a little bit more for women .	最重要的是 , 科學告訴我們 , 身為女性 , 最重要的是最好的科學告訴我們 , 身為女性 , 我的身體 , 你的身體 , 大概90年來 , 最重要的是最好的科學告訴我們 。
but life expectancy in this country is only 78 .	但在這個國家的壽命只有78歲
so somewhere along the line , we're leaving about 12 good years on the table .	在這條線上 , 我們留下了12個好年 。
these are years that we could get .	這些年來 , 我們能得到 。
and research shows that they would be years largely free of chronic disease , heart disease , cancer and diabetes .	研究顯示他們會在慢性疾病、心臟病、癌症和糖尿病中有多年 。
we think the best way to get these missing years is to look at the cultures around the world that are actually experiencing them , areas where people are living to age 100 at rates up to 10 times greater than we are , areas where the life expectancy is an extra dozen years , the rate of middle age mortality is a fraction of what it is in this country .	我們認為最好的方法就是去看那些在世界各地的文化 , 在那裡 , 年齡死亡率的人口數年 , 比我們所知的還要多年 , 年齡的數年齡死亡率高達10倍 , 比我們所知的還要多年齡 , 年齡死亡率高達10倍 。
we found our first blue zone about 125 miles off the coast of italy , on the island of sardinia .	我們發現了我們的第一個藍色區塊 , 大約125英里 , 來自西西亞的東岸 。
and not the entire island , the island is about 1 . 4 million people , but only up in the highlands , an area called the nuoro province .	而不是整個島嶼 , 島上有1400萬人 , 但只在高地 , 島上有1400萬人 , 但只有在高地 , 島上有一千四百萬人 。
and here we have this area where men live the longest , about 10 times more centenarians than we have here in america .	這裡有這個地區 , 美國人口的人口比我們還多 , 更長 , 大約10倍 。
and this is a place where people not only reach age 100 , they do so with extraordinary vigor .	這是一個地方 , 人們不只能到達100歲 , 他們也做得很好 。
places where 102 year olds still ride their bike to work , chop wood , and can beat a guy 60 years younger than them .	在那裡 , 十二歲的老年人仍然騎腳踏車去工作 , 玩家 , 比他們更年輕 。
their history actually goes back to about the time of christ .	他們的歷史其實回溯到聖誕節的時代 。
it's actually a bronze age culture that's been isolated .	其實是一塊古老的文化被孤立 。
because the land is so infertile , they largely are shepherds , which occasions regular , lowintensity physical activity .	因為土地是很大的 , 它們大大是羊群 , 牠們大小的身體活動 。
their diet is mostly plantbased , accentuated with foods that they can carry into the fields .	他們的飲食主要是植物為基礎的食物 , 他們的飲食是植物為基礎的 , 他們的飲食是植物為基礎的 。
they came up with an unleavened whole wheat bread called carta musica made out of durum wheat , a type of cheese made from grassfed animals so the cheese is high in omega3 fatty acids instead of omega6 fatty acids from cornfed animals , and a type of wine that has three times the level of polyphenols than any known wine in the world .	他們出發了一大堆肥胖的動物 , 一組成果 , 一種風力 , 一種風力 , 一種風力 , 一種風力 , 一種風力 , 一種風力 , 一種風力 , 一種風力 , 比任何非洲的風力都高 , 以至於三倍的溫度 , 比任何人都知風 。
but the real secret i think lies more in the way that they organize their society .	但真正的秘密我認為謊言是他們組織社會的秘密 。
and one of the most salient elements of the sardinian society is how they treat older people .	薩丁尼亞社會的一部分是他們如何治療老人 。
you ever notice here in america , social equity seems to peak at about age 24 ?	你注意到 , 在美國 , 社會平等似乎是24歲時會看到的嗎 ?
just look at the advertisements .	看看廣告 。
here in sardinia , the older you get the more equity you have , the more wisdom you're celebrated for .	在沙丁尼亞 , 老年人比較有智慧 , 你就越好了 。
you go into the bars in sardinia , instead of seeing the sports illustrated swimsuit calendar , you see the centenarian of the month calendar .	你走進巴西尼亞的山脈 , 看不到運動 , 去看運動 , 去看運動 , 去看運動 , 去看運動 , 去看運動 , 去看運動 , 去看運動 , 去看運動 , 去看運動 , 去看運動 , 去看運動 。
this , as it turns out , is not only good for your aging parents to keep them close to the family it imparts about four to six years of extra life expectancy research shows it's also good for the children of those families , who have lower rates of mortality and lower rates of disease .	事實證明 , 對於孩子們的家庭而言 , 不只適合他們的家人 , 更低率的死亡率和低率的死亡率 , 以及低率的死亡率和低率 。
that's called the grandmother effect .	這叫做 「 祖母效應 」 。
we found our second blue zone on the other side of the planet , about 800 miles south of tokyo , on the archipelago of okinawa .	我們發現我們的第二個藍色區域 , 大約800英里南 , 北京的南方 , 加州北部 。
okinawa is actually 161 small islands .	okinawa是161個小島 。
and in the northern part of the main island , this is ground zero for world longevity .	在主要島嶼的北部地區 , 這是地球上極端的一部分 。
this is a place where the oldest living female population is found .	這是最古老的居住女性族群 。
it's a place where people have the longest disabilityfree life expectancy in the world .	它是一個地方 , 人們在世界上最長的生命期待 , 不可思議 。
they have what we want .	他們有我們想要的 。
they live a long time , and tend to die in their sleep , very quickly , and often , i can tell you , after sex .	他們活得很快 , 通常 , 我可以告訴你 , 通常 , 我可以告訴你 , 死亡在睡眠中 , 很快地 , 通常 , 我可以告訴你 。
they live about seven good years longer than the average american .	他們比平均壽命更長 。
five times as many centenarians as we have in america .	美國有五倍 。
one fifth the rate of colon and breast cancer , big killers here in america .	第五分之一的乳癌、乳癌、乳癌 , 大殺人 。
and one sixth the rate of cardiovascular disease .	心血管疾病的四分之一 。
and the fact that this culture has yielded these numbers suggests strongly they have something to teach us .	這種文化的確有了這些數字建議 , 讓他們能教導我們 。
what do they do ?	他們會怎麼做 ?
once again , a plantbased diet , full of vegetables with lots of color in them .	一旦再一次 , 植物的飲食和許多顏色相互作用 。
and they eat about eight times as much tofu as americans do .	他們吃了八倍 , 像美國人一樣 。
more significant than what they eat is how they eat it .	更重要的是 , 牠們吃了什麼 。
they have all kinds of little strategies to keep from overeating , which , as you know , is a big problem here in america .	他們有各種各式各樣的策略 , 以保持在美國 , 例如你知道的 , 這是美國最大的問題 。
a few of the strategies we observed: they eat off of smaller plates , so they tend to eat fewer calories at every sitting .	我們觀察到的一些策略:他們吃掉少數的策略 , 例如 , 他們會吃少數的策略 , 例如 , 他們會吃少數的卡路里 。
instead of serving family style , where you can sort of mindlessly eat as you're talking , they serve at the counter , put the food away , and then bring it to the table .	不是保存家人 , 把食物放到桌上 , 然後把食物放進去 , 把食物放到桌上 。
they also have a 3 , 000yearold adage , which i think is the greatest sort of diet suggestion ever invented .	他們也有三千歲的老年人 , 我認為這是最偉大的飲食建議 。
it was invented by confucius .	它是由混亂的發明 。
and that diet is known as the hara , hatchi , bu diet .	這種飲食是哈拉、哈拉、哈拉、哈拉、霍亂 。
it's simply a little saying these people say before their meal to remind them to stop eating when their stomach is [80] percent full .	只是一個小說 , 那些人說話 , 要提醒他們 , 不要吃掉他們 , 只剩下八十歲的孩子 。
it takes about a half hour for that full feeling to travel from your belly to your brain .	它花了大約一半小時 , 完全感受到你的腦袋 。
and by remembering to stop at 80 percent it helps keep you from doing that very thing .	請記住 , 要停止80%的幫助 , 讓你做得更好 。
but , like sardinia , okinawa has a few social constructs that we can associate with longevity .	但 , 像薩丁尼亞 , 皮膚亞有一些社會建構 , 讓我們能與長壽的結合 。
we know that isolation kills .	我們知道暴力殺戮 。
fifteen years ago , the average american had three good friends .	五十年前 , 美國有三個好朋友 。
we're down to one and half right now .	我們現在要到達一半 。
if you were lucky enough to be born in okinawa , you were born into a system where you automatically have a half a dozen friends with whom you travel through life .	如果你很幸運 , 你就生出了一半的朋友 , 你出生在加州 , 你出生在海水 , 你出生在你的人生中 , 你出生了 。
they call it a moai . and if you're in a moai you're expected to share the bounty if you encounter luck , and if things go bad , child gets sick , parent dies , you always have somebody who has your back .	他們稱它為moai , 如果你在一個moai , 如果你在一個月球上 , 你總是有一位母親 , 如果你在一個月球上 , 就會有你的回饋 。
this particular moai , these five ladies have been together for 97 years .	這種特殊的母親 , 五位女士在97年後就開始了 。
their average age is 102 .	他們的平均年齡是102 。
typically in america we've divided our adult life up into two sections .	通常在美國 , 我們把我們的成年分成兩組 。
there is our work life , where we're productive .	我們有工作生活 , 我們有生產力 。
and then one day , boom , we retire .	有一天 , 我們退休 。
and typically that has meant retiring to the easy chair , or going down to arizona to play golf .	基本上 , 它的意思是要把小椅子放到阿里桑 , 或往亞里桑來到亞利桑 。
in the okinawan language there is not even a word for retirement .	在巴拉斯語中 , 沒有任何一個詞 , 來回復 。
instead there is one word that imbues your entire life , and that word is " ikigai . "	不論是 「 伊基加斯 」 的詞 , 那個詞是 「 伊基加 」 。
and , roughly translated , it means " the reason for which you wake up in the morning . "	翻譯的原因是: 「 你早上醒來的原因 。 」
for this 102yearold karate master , his ikigai was carrying forth this martial art .	在這102歲的克里斯特•馬斯特 , 他的三十二歲的凱特•馬斯特 , 他的伊基加斯特是帶著這個神秘的藝術 。
for this hundredyearold fisherman it was continuing to catch fish for his family three times a week .	為了這百年的漁民 , 牠的漁民會持續捕捉漁夫 , 讓他家三次 。
and this is a question . the national institute on aging actually gave us a questionnaire to give these centenarians .	這是個問題 , 美國國會議員會提出一個問題 , 來給予這些百分之八十的國家 。
and one of the questions , they were very culturally astute , the people who put the questionnaire .	其中一個問題是 , 他們是非常文化的 , 人們會問他們 。
one of the questions was , " what is your ikigai ? "	其中一個問題是: 「 你的ikigai是什麼 ? 」
they instantly knew why they woke up in the morning .	他們很明顯地知道為什麼他們在早晨醒來 。
for this 102 year old woman , her ikigai was simply her greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	在這102歲的女人 , 她的祖母是她偉大的祖父 。
two girls separated in age by 101 and a half years .	兩位女孩在101歲時就有2個女孩 。
and i asked her what it felt like to hold a greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	我問她 , 她覺得自己會覺得什麼樣子 , 像是要保持一個偉大的女兒 。
and she put her head back and she said , " it feels like leaping into heaven . "	她把她的頭帶回來 , 說: 「 感覺就像是跳進天堂 。 」
i thought that was a wonderful thought .	我覺得這是一個很棒的思想 。
my editor at geographic wanted me to find america's blue zone .	我編輯的編輯要我去找美國的藍色區域 。
and for a while we looked on the prairies of minnesota , where actually there is a very high proportion of centenarians .	一旦我們看到了尼蘇達州的專家 , 那裡有非常高的專家 。
but that's because all the young people left .	但那是因為所有的年輕人都離開了 。
so , we turned to the data again .	所以 , 我們轉移到資料上 。
and we found america's longestlived population among the seventhday adventists concentrated in and around loma linda , california .	我們發現美國最長的長期 , 住在洛瑪琳達加州 , 加州的七天之內 。
adventists are conservative methodists .	傳統主義者是保守主義者 。
they celebrate their sabbath from sunset on friday till sunset on saturday .	他們慶祝他們慶祝他們在星期五週日的夏日 , 星期六的日子 。
a " 24hour sanctuary in time , " they call it .	《24小時週日》 , 他們稱之為 。
and they follow five little habits that conveys to them extraordinary longevity , comparatively speaking .	他們追蹤了五個小習慣 , 讓他們很長壽 , 比較有說話 。
in america here , life expectancy for the average woman is 80 .	在美國 , 平均女性有八十歲 。
but for an adventist woman , their life expectancy is 89 .	但 , 身為女性 , 他們的壽命是89 。
and the difference is even more pronounced among men , who are expected to live about 11 years longer than their american counterparts .	差異在於美國人數的數量還多了11年 , 比他們的美國人數還要多 。
now , this is a study that followed about 70 , 000 people for 30 years .	這是一項研究 , 大約七萬人 , 大約七萬人 。
sterling study . and i think it supremely illustrates the premise of this blue zone project .	研究研究 , 我覺得它很明顯地說明了這個藍色區計畫的預期 。
this is a heterogeneous community .	這是個很棒的社區 。
it's white , black , hispanic , asian .	它是白人、黑人、白人、黑人、黑人 。
the only thing that they have in common are a set of very small lifestyle habits that they follow ritualistically for most of their lives .	他們唯一的習慣是一組非常小的習慣 , 他們的習慣常常是一群非常小的習慣 , 讓他們遵循著最常見的習慣 。
they take their diet directly from the bible .	他們把他們的飲食直接從聖經中直接 。
genesis: chapter one , verse [29] , where god talks about legumes and seeds , and on one more stanza about green plants , ostensibly missing is meat .	文字:章魚 , 上帝的演講 , 關於綠色植物 , 不論是肉類 , 都會吃掉肉 。
they take this sanctuary in time very serious .	他們在非常嚴肅的情況下 , 非常嚴肅 。
for 24 hours every week , no matter how busy they are , how stressed out they are at work , where the kids need to be driven , they stop everything and they focus on their god , their social network , and then , hardwired right in the religion , are nature walks .	每週每週 , 每週 , 不論他們是多麼忙碌 , 他們會停止一切 , 把他們放在上帝、社交網絡 , 不論他們是多麼忙碌 , 他們會停止一切 , 把他們放在上帝、社會網絡 , 並且他們在宗教上是大自然的走路 。
and the power of this is not that it's done occasionally , the power is it's done every week for a lifetime .	這種力量的力量是每週一生都沒有發生 。
none of it's hard . none of it costs money .	不需要錢 。
adventists also tend to hang out with other adventists .	傳統主義者也傾向於其他的傳統主義者 。
so , if you go to an adventist's party you don't see people swilling jim beam or rolling a joint .	所以 , 如果你去一個專家的派派 , 你不會看到人們穿著吉姆•貝姆或羅拉斯的一部分 。
instead they're talking about their next nature walk , exchanging recipes , and yes , they pray .	相反地 , 他們祈禱 。
but they influence each other in profound and measurable ways .	但它們會影響彼此的影響 , 同時也影響彼此的影響 。
this is a culture that has yielded ellsworth whareham .	這是一種文化 , 讓埃爾爾•沃哈姆 。
ellsworth whareham is 97 years old .	ellswharehareharehareharehareharehareharehareharehareharehareham97歲
he's a multimillionaire , yet when a contractor wanted 6 , 000 dollars to build a privacy fence , he said , " for that kind of money i'll do it myself . "	他是多萬元的錢 , 但當作者想要六千美元 , 讓他說: 「 為了那樣的錢 , 我會做自己 。 」
so for the next three days he was out shoveling cement , and hauling poles around .	所以 , 接下來三天 , 他穿著衣服 , 穿著衣服 , 穿著衣服 。
and predictably , perhaps , on the fourth day he ended up in the operating room .	預測 , 可能是 , 在第四天他在手術室內進行手術室 。
but not as the guy on the table ; the guy doing openheart surgery .	但不是在桌上 , 男子在桌子上做開頭手術 。
at 97 he still does 20 openheart surgeries every month .	在97歲時 , 每個月都有20個開頭手術 。
ed rawlings , 103 years old now , an active cowboy , starts his morning with a swim .	老鼠 , 十三歲 , 一隻游泳 , 每天早上游泳 。
and on weekends he likes to put on the boards , throw up rooster tails .	在週末 , 他喜歡把板子放進板子上 , 丟下樓梯 。
her grandson actually lives in the twin cities here .	她的祖先生在華盛頓的城市裡 。
she starts her day with lifting weights .	她從那天開始 , 開始了她的日子 。
she rides her bicycle .	她騎腳踏車 。
and then she gets in her rootbeer colored 1994 cadillac seville , and tears down the san bernardino freeway , where she still volunteers for seven different organizations .	接著 , 她還是志願者在1994年在聖伯丁州的路上 , 在那裡 , 她還是志願者有七個不同的組織 。
i've been on 19 hardcore expeditions .	我在19個艱難的旅程中 。
i'm probably the only person you'll ever meet who rode his bicycle across the sahara desert without sunscreen .	我可能是唯一能見過他在撒哈拉沙漠沒有陽光的人 。
but i'll tell you , there is no adventure more harrowing than riding shotgun with marge deton .	但我會告訴你們 , 沒有冒險比起火星的山丘還要多 。
" a stranger is a friend i haven't met yet ! " she'd say to me .	「 陌生人是個朋友 , 我還沒見過 , 她會跟我說 。 」
so , what are the common denominators in these three cultures ?	所以 , 這些三種文化中有什麼共同點 ?
what are the things that they all do ?	什麼是他們所做的事 ?
and we managed to boil it down to nine .	然後我們將它降到九點 。
in fact we've done two more blue zone expeditions since this and these common denominators hold true .	事實上 , 我們已經做了兩種藍色區域 , 因為這和這些共同的辯論 , 這些共同點的確保證據 。
and the first one , and i'm about to utter a heresy here , none of them exercise , at least the way we think of exercise .	首先 , 我要把這段影片放到這裡 , 不管他們練習 , 至少我們認為練習的方法 。
instead , they set up their lives so that they are constantly nudged into physical activity .	相反地 , 他們把它們的活性帶進身體活動中 。
these 100yearold okinawan women are getting up and down off the ground , they sit on the floor , 30 or 40 times a day .	這些百歲的女子在地面上下下 , 她們坐在地板上、30或40次 。
sardinians live in vertical houses , up and down the stairs .	西班牙人住在垂直的房子裡 , 下樓梯 。
every trip to the store , or to church or to a friend's house occasions a walk .	每一趟旅程、教堂、教堂、教堂或教堂 , 或去教堂 , 或去教堂 , 或是去教堂 , 或去教堂 , 或去教堂 ,
they don't have any conveniences .	他們沒有任何的證據 。
there is not a button to push to do yard work or house work .	沒有一個按鈕 , 按下按鈕 , 按下按鈕 , 去做標準的工作或房子 。
if they want to mix up a cake , they're doing it by hand .	如果他們想要混合蛋糕 , 他們會用手做 。
that burns calories just as much as going on the treadmill does .	燃燒卡路里的卡路里就越多了 。
when they do do intentional physical activity , it's the things they enjoy . they tend to walk , the only proven way to stave off cognitive decline , and they all tend to have a garden .	當他們做實體活動時 , 他們通常會走路 , 唯一的進步 , 就是他們享受的目標 , 只能從認知的角度來看 , 只有一個花園 。
they know how to set up their life in the right way so they have the right outlook .	他們知道如何把他們的生活放在正確的路上 , 所以他們有權利的權利 。
each of these cultures take time to downshift .	每個文化都需要時間轉變 。
the sardinians pray . the seventhday adventists pray .	薩丁尼亞人祈禱 , 七天的祈禱 。
the okinawans have this ancestor veneration .	okinawan有這種祖先的靈感
but when you're in a hurry or stressed out , that triggers something called the inflammatory response , which is associated with everything from alzheimer's disease to cardiovascular disease .	但當你在傷害或壓力時 , 會觸發出一種叫做 「 腫瘤症狀 」 的反應 , 它與所有來自阿茲海默症有關的疾病有關 。
when you slow down for 15 minutes a day you turn that inflammatory state into a more antiinflammatory state .	當你慢慢十五分鐘時 , 你就會轉動到一個更感染的狀態 。
they have vocabulary for sense of purpose , ikigai , like the okinawans .	他們有各種特定的目的 , 例如 「 海水 」 。
you know the two most dangerous years in your life are the year you're born , because of infant mortality , and the year you retire .	你知道你人生中最危險的一年 , 你的生命中 , 一年是你生出生的 , 因為嬰兒死亡率 , 年復一年 。
these people know their sense of purpose , and they activate in their life , that's worth about seven years of extra life expectancy .	這些人知道他們的人生 , 值得約七年的壽命 。
there's no longevity diet .	沒有長壽命 。
instead , these people drink a little bit every day , not a hard sell to the american population .	相反地 , 這些人每天都喝了一小塊 , 不是賣給美國人口 。
they tend to eat a plantbased diet .	他們會吃植物的飲食 。
doesn't mean they don't eat meat , but lots of beans and nuts .	不代表他們不吃肉 , 但很多豆子和營養 。
and they have strategies to keep from overeating , little things that nudge them away from the table at the right time .	他們有策略 , 讓它們從桌子上移動 , 讓它們從桌子上移動 。
and then the foundation of all this is how they connect .	結果是他們連結的基礎
they put their families first , take care of their children and their aging parents .	他們把他們的家人拿來 , 照顧他們的孩子和他們的家人 。
they all tend to belong to a faithbased community , which is worth between four and 14 extra years of life expectancy if you do it four times a month .	他們都傾向於信仰基礎社群 , 在4和14年的壽命中 , 每個月有四分之一 。
and the biggest thing here is they also belong to the right tribe .	最重要的是他們也屬於對部落 。
they were either born into or they proactively surrounded themselves with the right people .	他們是生長的 , 或他們將自己與右邊的人相對 。
we know from the framingham studies , that if your three best friends are obese there is a 50 percent better chance that you'll be overweight .	我們知道 , 如果你的三個最好的朋友都觀察到 , 如果你的三個最好的朋友都觀察到 , 如果你的三個最好的朋友都能觀察到 , 你就會有更好的機會 。
so , if you hang out with unhealthy people , that's going to have a measurable impact over time .	所以 , 如果你與不健康的人交談 , 那將會有很大的影響力 。
instead , if your friend's idea of recreation is physical activity , bowling , or playing hockey , biking or gardening , if your friends drink a little , but not too much , and they eat right , and they're engaged , and they're trusting and trustworthy , that is going to have the biggest impact over time .	相反的 , 如果你的朋友喝了一小塊 , 沒有太多 , 你的朋友喝了一小塊 , 但不太多 , 牠們會有著大量的影響 , 或花園 , 如果你的朋友喝了一小塊 , 但不太多 , 牠們會有大大的影響 。
diets don't work . no diet in the history of the world has ever worked for more than two percent of the population .	沒有飲食 , 沒有飲食在歷史上 , 世界各地的人口數量超過2% 。
exercise programs usually start in january ; they're usually done by october .	專案通常是從日本開始的 , 他們通常會在日本中開始 。
when it comes to longevity there is no short term fix in a pill or anything else .	當它進步到長壽時 , 沒有短短的詞彙 , 或其他東西 。
but when you think about it , your friends are longterm adventures , and therefore , perhaps the most significant thing you can do to add more years to your life , and life to your years . thank you very much .	但當你想想看 , 你的朋友是長期的冒險 , 或許最重要的是你能做的事 , 才能花更多年的時間去做 , 你的朋友是長期的冒險 , 或許你能做的最重要的事情 , 就是要花更多年的時間 。 謝謝你 。
ink that conducts electricity ; a window that turns from clear to opaque at the flip of a switch ; a jelly that makes music . all this stuff exists , and catarina mota says: it's time to play with it . mota leads us on a tour of surprising and cool new materials , and suggests that the way we'll figure out what they're good for is to experiment , tinker and have fun .	要用這個東西來玩 , 讓音樂有趣 。 所有這些東西都存在 , 卡塔里娜莫塔里娜莫塔說: 「 要玩耍 , 讓音樂有趣 。 」 「 讓音樂 」 和 「 美麗 」 的 「  」 和 「 新材料 」 的力量 , 和酷的新材料一樣 , 我們會想出什麼樣子 , 讓音樂有趣 。
creativity , design , technology	創造力、設計、科技 。
catarina mota: play with smart materials	catarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarinamotarina:
i have a friend in portugal whose grandfather built a vehicle out of a bicycle and a washing machine so he could transport his family .	我有一位朋友 , 他可以送他的家人 , 把他的家人拿來交通 。
he did it because he couldn't afford a car , but also because he knew how to build one .	他這麼做 , 因為他知道如何建造一個 。
there was a time when we understood how things worked and how they were made , so we could build and repair them , or at the very least make informed decisions about what to buy .	有時候 , 我們了解如何運作 , 並且修復它們 , 或至少在做些什麼是如何做的事 , 才能建造並修復它們 , 或至少在做些什麼是如何做的事 , 才能建造並修復它們 , 或至少在做些什麼是如何做的事 。
many of these doityourself practices were lost in the second half of the 20th century .	在20世紀中 , 許多人都在20世紀中失去了 。
but now , the maker community and the opensource model are bringing this kind of knowledge about how things work and what they're made of back into our lives , and i believe we need to take them to the next level , to the components things are made of .	但現在 , 創作者的社群和開放式的模型就是把它們帶到下一個層面 , 把它們帶到下一個層面 , 把它們帶到下一個層面 , 把它們轉化為我們的生活 , 我相信我們需要把它們帶到下一個層面 , 讓它們變成我們的生活 , 我相信我們需要把它們帶到下一個層面 , 讓它們變得更好 。
for the most part , we still know what traditional materials like paper and textiles are made of and how they are produced .	大部分的部分 , 我們仍然知道傳統的材料像是紙和紡織品 , 以及它們如何生產 。
but now we have these amazing , futuristic composites plastics that change shape , paints that conduct electricity , pigments that change color , fabrics that light up .	但現在我們有了這些驚人的生物 , 製造電力 , 製造電力 , 製造電力 , 製造電力 , 製造電力 , 製造電力 , 製造電力 , 製造電力 , 製造電力 , 製造電力 , 製造電力 , 讓它改變顏色 。
let me show you some examples .	讓我展示一些例子 。
so conductive ink allows us to paint circuits instead of using the traditional printed circuit boards or wires .	因此 , 使用傳統印刷電路板或線線 , 用傳統印刷電路板或線線 。
in the case of this little example i'm holding , we used it to create a touch sensor that reacts to my skin by turning on this little light .	在這個小例子中 , 我們用它來創造一個觸碰感應器 , 用它來創造一個觸碰感應器 , 用它來創造一個觸碰感應器 。
conductive ink has been used by artists , but recent developments indicate that we will soon be able to use it in laser printers and pens .	工藝學會用在雷射印刷機和鉛筆上 , 但最近的發展顯示 , 我們很快就能夠用它在雷射印刷機和鉛筆上 。
and this is a sheet of acrylic infused with colorless lightdiffusing particles .	這是一顆晶片 , 用顏色的光光化粒子來解放它 。
what this means is that , while regular acrylic only diffuses light around the edges , this one illuminates across the entire surface when i turn on the lights around it .	意思是 , 當光線穿越整個表面時 , 我會把光線轉換成光線 , 讓光線穿越整個表面 。
two of the known applications for this material include interior design and multitouch systems .	其中兩種都知道應用程式 , 包括設計和模擬系統 。
and thermochromic pigments change color at a given temperature .	氣候變色的顏色會改變顏色 。
so i'm going to place this on a hot plate that is set to a temperature only slightly higher than ambient and you can see what happens .	所以 , 我要把這個放在一個熱板上 , 讓它的溫度很高 , 且你可以看到它發生了什麼事 。
so one of the principle applications for this material is , amongst other things , in baby bottles , so it indicates when the contents are cool enough to drink .	這種材料的原則是 , 在寶寶瓶裡 , 其中一個原則是 , 在寶寶瓶子裡 , 牠們會很酷 。
so these are just a few of what are commonly known as smart materials .	這些只是少數幾個常常被稱為聰明的材料 。
in a few years , they will be in many of the objects and technologies we use on a daily basis .	幾年後 , 它們會在許多物體和技術上使用日常的物品和技術 。
we may not yet have the flying cars science fiction promised us , but we can have walls that change color depending on temperature , keyboards that roll up , and windows that become opaque at the flick of a switch .	我們可能還沒有飛行車 , 但我們可以有牆壁 , 改變顏色的溫度、鍵盤 , 以及窗戶 , 讓它轉變為光線 , 讓它可以改變顏色 。
so i'm a social scientist by training , so why am i here today talking about smart materials ?	我是一個社會科學家 , 所以為什麼我今天要來談智慧的材料 ?
well first of all , because i am a maker .	首先 , 因為我是作家 。
i'm curious about how things work and how they are made , but also because i believe we should have a deeper understanding of the components that make up our world , and right now , we don't know enough about these hightech composites our future will be made of .	我很好奇 , 對於這些高科技的成果是如何運作的 , 但也是因為我相信我們應該更深入了解它們是如何運作的 , 以及它們如何運作的 , 但也是因為我相信我們應該更深入了解它們是如何運作的 , 以及它們如何運作 , 而現在 , 我們不知道這些高科技的成果是如何運作的 。
smart materials are hard to obtain in small quantities .	聰明的材料很難在小量子中找到 。
there's barely any information available on how to use them , and very little is said about how they are produced .	幾乎沒有任何資訊可以使用它們 , 很小說他們是如何生產的 。
so for now , they exist mostly in this realm of trade secrets and patents only universities and corporations have access to .	所以 , 目前 , 大部分都在這個真實的貿易秘密和專利中 , 只有大學和企業都能取得 。
so a little over three years ago , kirsty boyle and i started a project we called open materials .	大約三年前 , 我開始了一個計畫叫做開放材料 。
it's a website where we , and anyone else who wants to join us , share experiments , publish information , encourage others to contribute whenever they can , and aggregate resources such as research papers and tutorials by other makers like ourselves .	它是個網站 , 包括我們 , 分享實驗 , 鼓勵其他人 , 想要加入我們 , 分享實驗 , 分享實驗 , 分享實驗 , 鼓勵其他人想要加入我們 , 分享實驗 , 鼓勵其他人想要加入我們 , 分享實驗 , 鼓勵其他人想要加入我們 , 分享實驗 , 鼓勵其他人想要加入我們 , 分享實驗 , 鼓勵其他人想要加入我們 , 分享實驗 , 鼓勵其他人想要加入我們 。
we would like it to become a large , collectively generated database of doityourself information on smart materials .	我們會喜歡它成為一個大型的資料庫 , 集體地創造出資料庫的資料庫 。
but why should we care how smart materials work and what they are made of ?	但 , 為什麼我們要照顧聰明的材料 , 以及他們在做什麼 ?
first of all , because we can't shape what we don't understand , and what we don't understand and use ends up shaping us .	首先 , 因為我們無法形塑我們不了解的 , 而我們不了解的 , 我們不了解 , 並用終結了我們 。
the objects we use , the clothes we wear , the houses we live in , all have a profound impact on our behavior , health and quality of life .	我們用的物品 , 衣服 , 衣服 , 衣服 , 衣服 , 衣服 , 衣服 , 衣服 , 衣服 , 衣服 , 衣服 , 衣服 , 衣服 , 衣服 , 衣服 , 衣服在我們
so if we are to live in a world made of smart materials , we should know and understand them .	所以 , 如果我們要活在一個充滿智慧的材料 , 我們應該知道 , 了解它們 。
secondly , and just as important , innovation has always been fueled by tinkerers .	第二 , 最重要的 , 創新總是被吸引者 。
so many times , amateurs , not experts , have been the inventors and improvers of things ranging from mountain bikes to semiconductors , personal computers , airplanes .	很多時候 , 沒有專家 , 那些發明家 , 不專家 , 進步 , 專家 , 遠離山腳踏車 , 進一步 , 專家 , 遠離山腳踏車 , 進一步 , 遠離山腳踏車 , 飛機 。
the biggest challenge is that material science is complex and requires expensive equipment .	最大的挑戰是 , 材料科學需要昂貴的設備 。
but that's not always the case .	但這並不總是如此 。
two scientists at university of illinois understood this when they published a paper on a simpler method for making conductive ink .	兩位科學家 , 在伊利諾州大學的一篇文章中 , 他們發表了一篇論文 , 用一個簡單的方法來做調查 。
jordan bunker , who had had no experience with chemistry until then , read this paper and reproduced the experiment at his maker space using only offtheshelf substances and tools .	jordanbunker曾沒有經歷過化學 , 直到那之後 , 閱讀這篇文章 , 用它的材料和工具來完成實驗 。
he used a toaster oven , and he even made his own vortex mixer , based on a tutorial by another scientist/maker .	他用了一座大麻醉 , 甚至製造了他的自己的創作者 , 由另一個科學家/maker所創作的 。
jordan then published his results online , including all the things he had tried and didn't work , so others could study and reproduce it .	jordan在網上搜尋了他的結果 , 包括所有他曾經嘗試過的結果 , 包括他所嘗試的一切 , 沒有工作 , 所以其他人可以研究並複製它 。
so jordan's main form of innovation was to take an experiment created in a wellequipped lab at the university and recreate it in a garage in chicago using only cheap materials and tools he made himself .	jordan主要的創新就是把一個實驗在芝加哥的一個實驗創造出一個實驗 , 在芝加哥使用唯一便宜的材料和工具 , 讓他自己做 。
and now that he published this work , others can pick up where he left and devise even simpler processes and improvements .	現在 , 他出版了這個工作 , 其他人可以選擇離開 , 其他可以挑選出版本 , 其他人可以選擇左邊 , 更簡單的過程和改善 。
another example i'd like to mention her project's goal is to highlight the expressive qualities of materials while focusing on the creativity and skills of the builder .	另外一個例子我想要提倡她專注於創造力和技能的創意和技能 。
electronics kits are very powerful in that they teach us how things work , but the constraints inherent in their design influence the way we learn .	電子裝置是非常強大的 , 因為他們教我們如何運作 , 但在他們的設計影響中 , 我們學習的方式是非常強大的 。
so hannah's approach , on the other hand , is to formulate a series of techniques for creating unusual objects that free us from predesigned constraints by teaching us about the materials themselves .	hannah的方法是 , 在另一方面 , 由於設計出一系列的技術 , 來創造出一種不尋常的物體 , 讓我們從未知的物體中取代 , 來創造出不尋常的物品 , 讓我們從未知的角度去做 , 來創造出不尋常的物品 。

so based on the research by marcelo coelho from mit , hannah created a series of paper speakers out of a wide range of materials from simple copper tape to conductive fabric and ink .	所以 , 根據來自麻省理工學院的研究 , 哈納 , 用簡單的銅板來製造出一系列的文章 , 用簡單的銅板來製造一系列的紙 , 用簡單的銅板來製造一系列紙 , 用簡單的銅板來製造一系列紙 。

but paper electronics is one of the most promising branches of material science in that it allows us to create cheaper and flexible electronics .	但紙電子是材料科學中最強大的部分之一 , 它讓我們能創造出更便宜且有彈性的電子 。
so hannah's artisanal work , and the fact that she shared her findings , opens the doors to a series of new possibilities that are both aesthetically appealing and innovative .	所以hannah的創作者有一系列的新可能性 , 讓門成為一系列的新可能性 , 讓門成為一系列的新可能性 , 讓門成為一系列的新可能性 。
so the interesting thing about makers is that we create out of passion and curiosity , and we are not afraid to fail .	有趣的是 , 我們害怕失敗 , 不害怕失敗 。
we often tackle problems from unconventional angles , and , in the process , end up discovering alternatives or even better ways to do things .	我們常常處理問題 , 在過程中 , 終於找到替代方案或更好的方法來做事情 。
so the more people experiment with materials , the more researchers are willing to share their research , and manufacturers their knowledge , the better chances we have to create technologies that truly serve us all .	所以 , 更多的研究人員願意分享他們的研究 , 更多的研究人員願意分享他們的知識 , 更好的機會 , 我們需要創造科技 , 更好的機會 , 我們必須創造出科技 , 讓更多的研究人員願意分享他們的知識 , 更好的機會 。
so i feel a bit as ted nelson must have when , in the early 1970s , he wrote , " you must understand computers now . "	我覺得有點像tednelson在1970年代早期 , 他寫: 「 你必須了解電腦 。 」
back then , computers were these large mainframes only scientists cared about , and no one dreamed of even having one at home .	之後 , 電腦是這些大型的主題 , 只有科學家關心 , 而沒有人夢想在家裡 。
so it's a little strange that i'm standing here and saying , " you must understand smart materials now . "	這有點奇怪 , 我站在這裡說: 「 你必須了解智慧材料 。 」
just keep in mind that acquiring preemptive knowledge about emerging technologies is the best way to ensure that we have a say in the making of our future .	請記住 , 心智技術是最好的方法 , 來確保我們在未來的知識是最好的方法 。
when we drive , we get into a glass bubble , lock the doors and press the accelerator , relying on our eyes to guide us even though we can only see the few cars ahead of and behind us . but what if cars could share data with each other about their position and velocity , and use predictive models to calculate the safest routes for everyone on the road ? jennifer healey imagines a world without accidents .	當我們開車時 , 我們就會進入一個玻璃泡泡 , 用預測模式來指導我們 , 儘管我們只能看到幾輛車子 , 但如果車子可以分享資料 , 用預測模式來指導我們 , 儘管我們只能看到幾輛車子 , 並且用預測模式來計算安全的路線 , 讓所有人都在路上 , 不意外地 , 只要車子可以分享資料 , 並且用預測模式來計算安全的路線 , 讓所有人在路上 , 不論是誰 ?
jennifer healey: if cars could talk , accidents might be avoidable	jenniferhaley:如果汽車可以說 , 意外可能是避免的 。
let's face it: driving is dangerous .	咱們來談一下:開車很危險 。
it's one of the things that we don't like to think about , but the fact that religious icons and good luck charms show up on dashboards around the world betrays the fact that we know this to be true .	我們不喜歡去思考 , 但事實上 , 宗教信仰和好運氣管道在世界各地的事實中 , 我們都不喜歡思考 , 但事實上 , 宗教信仰和好運查者在世界各地的事實證明我們知道這個事實 。
car accidents are the leading cause of death in people ages 16 to 19 in the united states leading cause of death and 75 percent of these accidents have nothing to do with drugs or alcohol .	車禍發生在美國造成死亡和75%的死亡率 , 造成死亡及75%的死亡率 , 不用藥品或酒精 。
no one can say for sure , but i remember my first accident .	沒有人可以說 , 但我記得我第一次發生的事 。
i was a young driver out on the highway , and the car in front of me , i saw the brake lights go on .	我是一位年輕的駕駛車 , 在我面前 , 我看到布拉克燈 。
i'm like , " okay , all right , this guy is slowing down , i'll slow down too . "	我說: 「 好吧 , 這傢伙慢慢下來 , 我會慢下來 。 」
i step on the brake .	我踏上腳踏 。
but no , this guy isn't slowing down .	但不 , 這傢伙不會慢慢下來 。
this guy is stopping , dead stop , dead stop on the highway .	這傢伙停止 , 死停 , 停下來 , 停下來 , 停下來 , 死停下來 。
it was just going 65 to zero ?	只有65到0 ?
i slammed on the brakes .	我在布拉克上打電話 。
i felt the abs kick in , and the car is still going , and it's not going to stop , and i know it's not going to stop , and the air bag deploys , the car is totaled , and fortunately , no one was hurt .	我知道它不會停下來 , 我知道它不會停下來 , 我知道它不會停下來 , 我知道它不會停下來 , 我知道它不會停下來 , 我知道它不會停下來 , 汽車仍然會停下來 , 我知道它不會停下來 , 火車仍然會停下來 , 車子仍然會停下來 , 我知道它不會停下來 , 車子還會停下來 , 車子仍然會停下來 , 我知道它不會停下來 。

medical animator david bolinsky presents 3 minutes of stunning animation that show the bustling life inside a cell .	醫療保障者大衛•波林斯特在一個細胞內完成了三分鐘的刺激 。

and while these are both wonderful things in their own right they both have very wonderful things going for them truth and beauty as ideals that can be looked at by the sciences and by math are almost like the ideal conjoined twins that a scientist would want to date .	雖然這兩者都很美好 , 因為他們對科學和美麗的理想有著非常美好的理想 , 因為他們對科學和美麗的理想有著非常美好的理想 , 是因為科學和美麗的理想 , 由於科學和美麗的理想 , 可以被科學和美麗的理想結合在一起 。

they are things that describe beauty in a way that is often only accessible if you understand the language and the syntax of the person who studies the subject in which truth and beauty is expressed .	他們是用一種方式來描述美麗的事物 , 只要你了解語言和美麗的語言 , 和美麗的語言和美麗的表現 。

and what i've tried to do since i had my training as a medical illustrator since i was taught animation by my father , who was a sculptor and my visual mentor i wanted to figure out a way to help people understand truth and beauty in the biological sciences by using animation , by using pictures , by telling stories so that the things that are not necessarily evident to people can be brought forth , and can be taught , and can be understood .	自從我從我身為一名醫學學科醫學院 , 我想要找出一種方法來幫助人們了解真相和美麗 , 透過用圖像 , 來幫助人們了解真相和美麗 , 透過用圖像 , 來幫助人們了解真相和美麗 , 透過用圖像 , 來幫助人們了解真相和美麗 , 透過用圖像 , 來幫助人們了解真相和美麗 , 透過用圖像 , 來幫助人們了解真相和美麗 , 以便能被視覺導向 , 來幫助人們了解真相和美麗 , 透過用圖像 , 來幫助人們了解真相和美麗 , 透過用圖像 , 來幫助人們了解真相和美麗 。
students today are often immersed in an environment where what they learn is subjects that have truth and beauty embedded in them , but the way they're taught is compartmentalized and it's drawn down to the point where the truth and beauty are not always evident .	現今 , 學生通常會在環境中學習 , 但他們教學的內容是很有真相和美好的 , 但他們教學的內容是很有真相和美麗的 , 不是總是證據 。

and i had a telephone call from robert lue at harvard , in the molecular and cellular biology department , a couple of years ago . he asked me if my team and i would be interested and willing to really change how medical and scientific education is done at harvard .	我有一個電話叫robertluehrvard , 在哈佛大學 , 幾年前 , 他問我 , 如果我的團隊 , 我會很感興趣 , 並將真正改變醫學和科學教育在哈佛大學 。
so we embarked on a project that would explore the cell that would explore the truth and beauty inherent in molecular and cellular biology so that students could understand a larger picture that they could hang all of these facts on .	於是我們開始研究這個計畫 , 讓學生可以了解更大的圖片 , 可以了解更大的圖片 , 可以讓學生能了解更大的圖片 , 可以讓學生能了解更大的圖片 , 可以讓學生能了解更大的圖片 , 讓學生能了解更大的圖片 , 可以讓學生能了解更大的圖片 。

and these micromachines really are at the heart of life .	這些微型動物其實是生命的心臟 。
these micromachines , which are the envy of nanotechnologists the world over , are selfdirected , powerful , precise , accurate devices that are made out of strings of amino acids .	這些微生物 , 是一種自動化、強大、精確、精確的裝置 , 由強力、精準、精確的裝置 , 由於強大、精確、精確的裝置 。

and so what we wanted to do was to figure out how we could make this story into an animation that would be the centerpiece of biovisions at harvard , which is a website that harvard has for its molecular and cellular biology students that will in addition to all the textual information , in addition to all the didactic stuff put everything together visually , so that these students would have an internalized view of what a cell really is in all of its truth and beauty , and be able to study with this view in mind , so that their imaginations would be sparked , so that their passions would be sparked and so that they would be able to go on and use these visions in their head to make new discoveries and to be able to find out , really , how life works .	所以我們想做的是 , 我們想要做的是 , 把所有東西都放在一起 , 用這些視覺來研究這個觀點 , 讓這些學生可以在哈佛身上找到 , 真正的生物學學學生 , 將這些視覺傳遞給所有資訊 , 讓這些學生可以在哈佛身上學習 , 用這些視覺來研究 , 這樣 , 他們的智慧會被激發 , 所以 , 這些學生會被傳達出來 , 這樣 , 他們的智慧會被傳播 , 所以 , 這些學生會被傳遞到 , 這樣他們才能找到真正的生命 , 這樣 , 才能找到真正的生命 , 這樣 , 才能找到真正的生命 。

we worked with a theme , which is , you've got macrophages that are streaming down a capillary , and they're touching the surface of the capillary wall , and they're picking up information from cells that are on the capillary wall , and they are given this information that there's an inflammation somewhere outside , where they can't see and sense .	我們用了一個標題 , 上面有一塊藍色的圖片 , 上面有一堆紅外線 , 它們會在牆壁上發出這些訊息 , 在那裡 , 它們會被吸引到附近的水面 , 在那裡 , 它們會被吸引到附近的水面 , 在那裡 , 牠們會看到和感知 。

and so what i'm going to show you is a threeminute reader's digest version of the first aspect of this film that we produced . it's an ongoing project that's going to go another four or five years .	接下來我要給各位看的是 , 我們製作的第一張照片 , 是一台關於我們製作的第一張照片 , 它是一台三分鐘的資料 , 是我們所製造的 , 這部電影所產生的一部分 , 是我們所製造的 , 它是一台三分鐘的電腦 , 將來到另一個四或五年 。

run the movie , please .	拍電影 , 拜託 。
but these machines that power the inside of the cells are really quite amazing , and they really are the basis of all life because all of these machines interact with each other .	但這些機器在細胞內部的功能非常驚人 , 它們真的是非常棒的 , 因為這些機器都與彼此互動 。

and the cell will actually manufacture the parts that it needs on the fly , from information that's brought from the nucleus by molecules that read the genes .	細胞會製造出這些細胞的部分 , 從資訊從核子的分子中 , 從資訊從核子傳送到基因 。
no life , from the smallest life to everybody here , would be possible without these little micromachines .	沒有這些小小的生命 , 從最小的生命 , 到每個人 , 可能沒有這些小小的生命 。
in fact , it would really , in the absence of these machines , have made the attendance here , chris , really quite sparse .	事實上 , 在這些機器中 , 克里斯 , 真的很令人驚訝 。
this is the fedex delivery guy of the cell .	這是fedexdelit細胞的病人 。
this little guy is called the kinesin , and he pulls a sack that's full of brand new manufactured proteins to wherever it's needed in the cell whether it's to a membrane , whether it's to an organelle , whether it's to build something or repair something .	這個小傢伙叫做kinesin , 他推出了一系列的新製造蛋白質 , 它是用來製造蛋白質 , 或修復它 。
and each of us has about 100 , 000 of these things running around , right now , inside each one of your 100 trillion cells .	現在 , 每個人都有大約一萬四十萬個這些東西 , 現在 , 在每個人當中 , 大約有一千萬個這些東西 , 現在 , 在你一百兆個細胞中 。
so no matter how lazy you feel , you're not really intrinsically doing nothing .	所以 , 不論你有多瘋狂 , 你其實沒有什麼 。

becky blanton planned to live in her van for a year and see the country , but when depression set in and her freelance job ended , her camping trip turned into homelessness . in this intimate talk , she describes her experience of becoming one of america's working homeless .	貝克•布蘭頓計劃在她的生活中 , 去年復活 , 但當憂鬱症和她所經歷的經歷成為美國人工作時 , 她的經歷卻是無家可歸的 。
adventure , happiness , life , personal growth , poverty , social change , society , storytelling	冒險、快樂、生活、個人成長、貧窮、社會變革、社會變革、社會變革、社會變革、社會變革、社會變革、社會變革、社會變革、社會、
becky blanton: the year i was homeless	貝琪•布蘭頓:一年我無家可歸 。
i'm a writer and a journalist , and i'm also an insanely curious person , so in 22 years as a journalist , i've learned how to do a lot of new things .	我是個作家和記者 , 我知道如何做很多新的事 。
and three years ago , one of the things i learned how to do was to become invisible .	三年前 , 我學到的是要成為隱形 。
i became one of the working homeless .	我成為了無家可歸的人 。
i quit my job as a newspaper editor after my father died in february of that same year , and decided to travel .	我辭職了一份報紙 , 決定要去旅行 。
his death hit me pretty hard .	他的命令我非常困難 。
and there were a lot of things that i wanted to feel and deal with while i was doing that .	有許多東西我想要感受和處理 , 當我在做這件事時 。
i've camped my whole life . and i decided that living in a van for a year to do this would be like one long camping trip .	我花了一輩子 , 我決定住在一個長期營養的旅程中 , 我決定住在一個長營的旅程中 。
so i packed my cat , my rottweiler and my camping gear into a 1975 chevy van , and drove off into the sunset , having fully failed to realize three critical things .	所以 , 我把我的貓帶到我的貓上 , 我把我的貓帶到我的洞穴裡 , 把我的貓帶到1975年 , 完全失敗了 , 完全失敗了這三個關鍵的事情 。
one: that society equates living in a permanent structure , even a shack , with having value as a person .	第一:社會平均生活在永久的結構上 , 甚至是一群人 , 甚至是一群人 , 甚至是一群人 。
two: i failed to realize how quickly the negative perceptions of other people can impact our reality , if we let it .	第二:我失敗了 , 了解到他人能影響我們的現實 , 如果我們讓他人能影響我們的現實 。
three: i failed to realize that homelessness is an attitude , not a lifestyle .	第三:我失敗了 , 意識到無家可歸是一種態度 , 而不是生活方式 。
at first , living in the van was great .	首先 , 生活在空中很棒 。
i showered in campgrounds . i ate out regularly .	我在校園裡演出 , 通常 , 我會飛行 。
and i had time to relax and to grieve .	我有時間放鬆和悲傷 。
but then the anger and the depression about my father's death set in .	但 , 憤怒和憂鬱症 , 是我父親的死刑 。
my freelance job ended . and i had to get a fulltime job to pay the bills .	我的工作結束了 , 我必須得到一個全職的薪水 。
what had been a really mild spring turned into a miserably hot summer .	當時是非常熱夏天的夏天 。
and it became impossible to park anywhere without being very obvious that i had a cat and a dog with me , and it was really hot .	沒有很明顯地 , 我有一隻貓和一隻貓 , 一隻貓和一隻貓 , 我有一隻貓和一隻貓 , 我有一隻貓和一隻貓 , 跟我一樣 , 很明顯 。
the cat came and went through an open window in the van .	貓來了 , 開了一扇窗戶 。
the doggy went into doggy day care .	這隻狗在狗狗上去了狗 。
whenever i could , i used employee showers in office buildings and truck stops .	每當我可以 , 我用員工在辦公室大樓和卡車停下來 。
or i washed up in public rest rooms .	或我在公共場的房間裡 。
nighttime temperatures in the van rarely dropped below 80 degrees fahrenheit , making it difficult or impossible to sleep .	夜晚的溫度降低80度的溫度 , 讓它很難或不可能睡眠 。
food rotted in the heat .	食物在熱中 。
ice in my ice chest melted within hours , and it was pretty miserable .	我冰箱在幾小時內的冰箱裡冰冷 , 而且它很糟 。
i couldn't afford to find an apartment , or couldn't afford an apartment that would allow me to have the rottweiler and the cat .	我無法負擔得起一個公寓 , 或無法負擔得起公寓 , 或無法負擔得起公寓 , 或無法負擔得起公寓 , 或無法負擔得起公寓 , 或無法負擔得起公寓 。
and i refused to give them up , so i stayed in the van .	我拒絕給他們放棄 , 所以我留下了 。
and when the heat made me too sick to walk the 50 feet to the public restroom outside my van at night , i used a bucket and a trash bag as a toilet .	當熱情讓我太生病時 , 我用一塊垃圾桶 , 用一桶垃圾桶 , 用一桶垃圾桶和垃圾桶 。
when winter weather set in , the temperatures dropped below freezing . and they stayed there .	當冬天氣溫降低時 , 溫度會降低 , 溫度降低 , 溫度降低 , 溫度降低了 , 溫度降低了 。
and i faced a whole new set of challenges .	我面對了一個全新的挑戰 。
i parked a different place every night so i would avoid being noticed and hassled by the police .	每天晚上 , 我會避免注意到 , 被警察打開 。
i didn't always succeed .	我並不總是成功 。
but i felt out of control of my life .	但我感覺到我的人生 。
and i don't know when or how it happened , but the speed at which i went from being a talented writer and journalist to being a homeless woman , living in a van , took my breath away .	我不知道何時發生什麼事 , 但是我從一名無家可歸者和記者 , 帶著我的呼吸 , 走進去 。
i hadn't changed . my i . q . hadn't dropped .	我沒有改變 , 我的智商 , 沒有改變 。 我的智商沒有改變 。
my talent , my integrity , my values , everything about me remained the same .	我的價值觀、我的價值觀、我的價值觀 , 所有我都一樣 。
but i had changed somehow .	但我已經改變了 。
i spiraled deeper and deeper into a depression .	我深入憂鬱症 。
and eventually someone referred me to a homeless health clinic .	最後有人提醒我到一個無家的健康診所 。
and i went . i hadn't bathed in three days .	我去了 , 三天後 , 我沒有廁所 。
i was as smelly and as depressed as anyone in line .	我很像任何人一樣 , 身為任何人 。
i just wasn't drunk or high .	我只是不喝或高 。
and when several of the homeless men realized that , including a former university professor , they said , " you aren't homeless . why are you really here ? "	當幾位無家可歸的人意識到 , 包括一位前大學教授 , 他們說: 「 你不是家人 。 為什麼你在這裡 ? 」
other homeless people didn't see me as homeless , but i did .	其他無家可歸的家人都看不見我 , 但是我做了 。
then the professor listened to my story and he said , " you have a job . you have hope .	教授們聽我的故事 , 他說: 「 你有工作 , 你有希望 。
the real homeless don't have hope . "	真正的家人沒有希望 。 」
a reaction to the medication the clinic gave me for my depression left me suicidal . and i remember thinking , " if i killed myself , no one would notice . "	反對我的憂鬱症患者 , 我心想: 「 如果我殺了自己 , 沒有人會注意到 。 」
a friend told me , shortly after that , that she had heard that tim russert , a nationally renowned journalist , had been talking about me on national t . v .	一位朋友告訴我 , 她剛剛說過 , 她聽過這位女士 , 一個全國性的記者 , 她聽說過 , 一名全國性的記者 , 一直在談論我 , 一個國家的記者 , 一直在談論我 。
an essay i'd written about my father , the year before he died , was in tim's new book .	我寫了一篇關於我父親的故事 , 在他死前的一年 , 在他死前 , 在他死去 , 在他死去 , 在他死去 , 在他死去 , 在他死去 , 在他死去 。
and he was doing the talk show circuit . and he was talking about my writing .	他在談我的寫作 , 他在談論我的寫作 。
and when i realized that tim russert , former moderator of " meet the press , " was talking about my writing , while i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , i started laughing .	當我意識到 , 《大屠殺》 , 我開始笑話 , 我開始笑聲 。
i started laughing because it got to the point where , was i a writer , or was i a homeless woman ?	我開始笑了 , 因為它到哪裡 , 還是我是一位作家 , 或是我是無家可歸的女性 ?
so i went in the bookstore . and i found tim's book .	所以我去了書 , 我發現了tim的書 。
and i stood there . and i reread my essay .	我站在那裡 , 我把我丟掉了 。
because i was a writer .	因為我是作家 。
i was a writer .	我是作家 。
shortly after that i moved back to tennessee .	短短之後 , 我搬回去密度 。
i alternated between living in a van and couch surfing with friends .	我住在一個美麗的社區 , 與朋友一起吃飯 。
and i started writing again .	我開始寫作 。
by the summer of the following year i was a working journalist .	去年夏天 , 我是一位記者 。
i was winning awards . i was living in my own apartment .	我是贏得獎勵 , 我在自己的公寓裡 。
i was no longer homeless .	我不再無家可歸 。
and i was no longer invisible .	我不再隱形 。

author and activist isabel allende discusses women , creativity , the definition of feminism and , of course , passion in this talk .	作者和行動主義者也對女性主義的定義是女性主義的定義 , 當然 , 熱情 。
entertainment , global issues , love , parenting , storytelling , women , world cultures	娛樂 , 全球議題 , 女性 , 世界文化 , 說故事 , 女人 , 世界文化 。
isabel allende tells tales of passion	阿拉伯爾•阿拉伯爾•所有人都說了關於熱情的熱情 。
thank you so much . it's really scary to be here among the smartest of the smart .	謝謝你 , 非常可怕 , 很可怕 , 很可怕 。
i'm here to tell you a few tales of passion .	我在這裡要告訴各位一些關於熱情的熱情 。
there's a jewish saying that i love .	有個猶太人說我喜歡 。
what is truer than truth ? answer: the story .	真相是什麼 ? 答案:故事 。
i'm a storyteller . i want to convey something that is truer than truth about our common humanity .	我是說故事者 , 我想要說 , 對於我們共同的人性來說 , 比真相更真實 。
all stories interest me , and some haunt me until i end up writing them .	所有故事都很感興趣我 , 直到我最後寫了一篇故事 。
certain themes keep coming up: justice , loyalty , violence , death , political and social issues , freedom .	某些人會持續下去:正義、死亡、政治和社會議題 , 自由 。
i'm aware of the mystery around us , so i write about coincidences , premonitions , emotions , dreams , the power of nature , magic .	我意識到我們周遭的力量 , 所以我寫了關於自然、神秘、情緒、夢想、神秘的力量 。
in the last 20 years i have published a few books , but i have lived in anonymity until february of 2006 , when i carried the olympic flag in the winter olympics in italy .	過去二十年來 , 我在2006年出版了一些書 , 但是我在2006年出版了幾本書 , 當時我在2006年出版了幾本書 , 當時我在奧林匹克州冬天奧林匹克市的奧林匹克市中心工作 。
that made me a celebrity . now people recognize me in macy's , and my grandchildren think that i'm cool .	這使我很酷 。 現在人們認同我的孫子認為我很酷 。
allow me to tell you about my four minutes of fame .	讓我來告訴你我四分鐘的信息 。
one of the organizers of the olympic ceremony , of the opening ceremony , called me and said that i had been selected to be one of the flagbearers .	奧運的軍隊之一 , 叫做我 , 叫做我 , 叫做我 , 叫做我 , 叫做我 , 叫做我 , 叫做我 , 叫做我 , 叫我被選為一個旗幟 。
i replied that surely this was a case of mistaken identity because i'm as far as you can get from being an athlete .	我複製了 , 不論是錯誤的身分 , 我也不敢說 , 因為我身為一個運動員 , 你能成為運動員 。
actually , i wasn't even sure that i could go around the stadium without a walker .	實際上 , 我甚至不確定我可以在店裡沒有走路 。
i was told that this was no laughing matter .	我被告知這不是笑話 。
this would be the first time that only women would carry the olympic flag .	這是第一次 , 唯一女性會帶著奧林匹克旗幟 。
five women , representing five continents , and three olympic gold medal winners .	五個女性 , 代表五個大陸 , 還有三位奧林匹克•奧林匹克 。
my first question was , naturally , what was i going to wear ?	我的第一個問題是 , 天然 , 我要穿什麼 ?
a uniform , she said , and asked for my measurements .	她說 , 她說 , 請求我的測量 。
i had a vision of myself in a fluffy anorak , looking like the michelin man .	我有一份視覺 , 看起來像米爾•曼 。
by the middle of february , i found myself in turin , where enthusiastic crowds cheered when any of the 80 olympic teams was in the street .	由於 , 我在街上發現我自己在洛杉磯 , 當時在街上有80個奧運隊員在街上 。
those athletes had sacrificed everything to compete in the games .	那些運動員在遊戲中扮演了重要的角色 。
they all deserved to win , but there's the element of luck .	他們都保持贏 , 但那是幸運的 。
a speck of snow , an inch of ice , the force of the wind , can determine the result of a race or a game .	一片玻璃 , 風力的風力 , 風力的風力 , 可以決定結果是風力 , 或是一個遊戲 。
however , what matters most more than training or luck is the heart .	然而 , 最重要的比訓練或幸運是心臟 。

the year is 1998 , the place is a prison camp for tutsi refugees in congo .	今年是1998年 , 地方是一間監獄營 , 在那裡 , 一個囚犯在芝加哥的貧民區 。

she's pregnant and a widow .	她懷孕了 。

mapendo , in swahili , means great love .	在西班牙語中 , 意思是很棒的愛 。

i was born in ancient times , at the end of the world , in a patriarchal catholic and conservative family .	我出生於古老的時代 , 在世界各地 , 最後 , 在這個世界的最後 , 一個專利和保守派的家庭 。

i think that the time is ripe to make fundamental changes in our civilization .	我認為 , 時間在我們的文明中創造基礎改變 。
but for real change , we need feminine energy in the management of the world .	但 , 為了真正的改變 , 我們需要女性的能源 , 來解決世界 。
we need a critical number of women in positions of power , and we need to nurture the feminine energy in men .	我們需要培養女性的女性權力 , 我們需要培養女性的女性權力 。
i'm talking about men with young minds , of course .	我在談的是男人 , 當然 。
old guys are hopeless ; we have to wait for them to die off .	老人無希望 , 我們必須等待他們死掉 。
yes , i would love to have sophia loren's long legs and legendary breasts .	是的 , 我很喜歡有蘇菲亞洛倫的長腿和法律 。
but given a choice , i would rather have the warrior hearts of wangari maathai , somaly mam , jenny and rose mapendo .	但 , 為了選擇 , 我會有選擇 , 我會和羅斯•馬利•馬蒂娜和羅斯•馬特•馬利•馬特爾•馬特 。
i want to make this world good .	我想要讓這個世界變得好 。
not better , but to make it good .	不好 , 但要讓它好好 。
why not ? it is possible . look around in this room all this knowledge , energy , talent and technology .	為什麼不呢 ? 它可能在這個房間裡 , 所有的知識、能源、科技 。
let's get off our fannies , roll up our sleeves and get to work , passionately , in creating an almost perfect world .	咱們來把我們的腳踏進去 , 創造一個幾乎完美的世界 。
every day , in a city the size of london , 30 million meals are served . but where does all the food come from ? architect carolyn steel discusses the daily miracle of feeding a city , and shows how ancient food routes shaped the modern world .	每天 , 每一天 , 一座城市的城市 , 一座城市的大小 , 大約有三千萬美元的食物 , 但從哪裡來 , 建築師卡羅倫•史蒂爾討論了一座城市的大小 , 顯示古代的食物是如何形狀現代世界的 。
cities , culture , food , global issues	城市、文化、食物、全球議題 。
carolyn steel: how food shapes our cities	卡羅倫•史蒂:我們如何塑造我們的城市 , 如何塑造我們的城市 。
how do you feed a city ?	你要如何餵飽一個城市 ?
it's one of the great questions of our time .	這是我們時代最棒的問題之一 。
yet it's one that's rarely asked .	然而 , 它是很罕見的 。
we take it for granted that if we go into a shop or restaurant , or indeed into this theater's foyer in about an hour's time , there is going to be food there waiting for us , having magically come from somewhere .	我們要把它放進去 , 或餐廳 , 或餐廳 , 或餐廳 , 或餐廳 , 或餐廳 , 或餐廳 , 或餐廳 , 或餐廳 , 等著我們 , 到一個小時的時期 , 將食物等待我們 。
but when you think that every day for a city the size of london , enough food has to be produced , transported , bought and sold , cooked , eaten , disposed of , and that something similar has to happen every day for every city on earth , it's remarkable that cities get fed at all .	但當你認為每一天城市都市大小 , 都市長大小 , 都市大小 , 大小的城市 , 都市長大小 , 大小的城市 , 都市長大小 , 大小的信念 , 大小的城市 , 都市長大小 , 大小的城市 , 都被運輸、買賣、煮飯、煮飯、吃掉 , 甚至不太一樣 。
we live in places like this as if they're the most natural things in the world , forgetting that because we're animals and that we need to eat , we're actually as dependent on the natural world as our ancient ancestors were .	我們生活在自然世界中 , 如同我們所熟悉的自然世界一樣 , 因為我們是動物 , 而我們需要吃 , 我們其實是自然世界的人類 , 以致於人類的自然世界 , 成為人類的祖先 。
and as more of us move into cities , more of that natural world is being transformed into extraordinary landscapes like the one behind me it's soybean fields in mato grosso in brazil in order to feed us .	隨著更多人搬進城市裡 , 自然世界會被轉化成非凡的景像 , 像我在巴西的土地景像 , 把我們帶到城市裡 。
these are extraordinary landscapes , but few of us ever get to see them .	這些是非凡的景觀 , 但少數人看到他們 。
and increasingly these landscapes are not just feeding us either .	令人驚訝的是這些地景並不只是讓我們的地景 。
as more of us move into cities , more of us are eating meat , so that a third of the annual grain crop globally now gets fed to animals rather than to us human animals .	隨著更多人搬進城市裡 , 我們吃肉 , 比人類的動物還要多 。
and given that it takes three times as much grain actually ten times as much grain to feed a human if it's passed through an animal first , that's not a very efficient way of feeding us .	若有三倍之多 , 人類就不太有效率地餵飽人類 , 這不是很有效的餵食方式 。
and it's an escalating problem too .	這也是一場災難的問題 。
by 2050 , it's estimated that twice the number of us are going to be living in cities .	到了2050年 , 估計 , 估計人口數量的人口數量是住在城市中 。
and it's also estimated that there is going to be twice as much meat and dairy consumed .	它也估計 , 要有兩倍的肉和毛毛 , 會被消耗掉 。
so meat and urbanism are rising hand in hand .	肉類和城市主義都在手上 。
and that's going to pose an enormous problem .	這會帶來一個巨大的問題 。
six billion hungry carnivores to feed , by 2050 .	六十億個飢餓的卡尼佛 , 到2050年 。
that's a big problem . and actually if we carry on as we are , it's a problem we're very unlikely to be able to solve .	這是個很大的問題 , 如果我們帶著我們去解決這個問題 , 真的很不可思議 。
nineteen million hectares of rainforest are lost every year to create new arable land .	每年有九十萬公頃的雨林 , 都失去了每一年 , 創造新的可可居住地 。
although at the same time we're losing an equivalent amount of existing arables to salinization and erosion .	儘管如此 , 我們也失去了一份很有用的證據 , 可以用在同一時間 , 用在同一時間 , 我們失去了一份保存性 , 來保持清晰和氧氣 。
we're very hungry for fossil fuels too .	我們對化石燃料非常渴望 。
it takes about 10 calories to produce every calorie of food that we consume in the west .	它需要大約10種卡路里 , 來生產我們消費的食物 。
and even though there is food that we are producing at great cost , we don't actually value it .	儘管我們有食物 , 我們也沒有價值它 。
half the food produced in the usa is currently thrown away .	一半的食物生產在美國現在被丟棄了 。
and to end all of this , at the end of this long process , we're not even managing to feed the planet properly .	最後 , 在這個長程的過程中 , 我們甚至沒有辦法讓地球飛行 。
a billion of us are obese , while a further billion starve .	數十億個人類是肥胖 , 更有十億人是肥胖的 。
none of it makes very much sense .	沒有任何東西都很有意義 。
and when you think that 80 percent of global trade in food now is controlled by just five multinational corporations , it's a grim picture .	當你認為百分之八十的全球貿易現在已經被控制了五個多國公司 , 這是一張圖片 。
as we're moving into cities , the world is also embracing a western diet .	當我們搬進城市時 , 世界也擁抱西方飲食 。
and if we look to the future , it's an unsustainable diet .	如果我們看看未來 , 它是一個永續的飲食 。
so how did we get here ?	所以 , 我們怎麼辦到呢 ?
and more importantly , what are we going to do about it ?	更重要的是 , 我們要怎麼做 ?
well , to answer the slightly easier question first , about 10 , 000 years ago , i would say , is the beginning of this process in the ancient near east , known as the fertile crescent .	首先 , 我會說 , 一萬年前 , 我會說 , 一萬年前 , 剛剛剛剛剛剛提到的一萬年前 , 我會說 , 第一 , 一萬年前 , 我會說 , 這是在古老近東的一萬年前 , 被稱為 「 冰河流程 」 。
because , as you can see , it was crescent shaped .	因為 , 如你所見 , 它是creen的形狀 。
and it was also fertile .	它也很有彈性 。
and it was here , about 10 , 000 years ago , that two extraordinary inventions , agriculture and urbanism , happened roughly in the same place and at the same time .	大約一萬年前 , 這兩種非凡的發明、農業和城市主義 , 發生在同一個地方 。
this is no accident , because agriculture and cities are bound together . they need each other .	這不是意外的 , 因為農業和城市都融合在一起 , 他們需要彼此 。
because it was discovery of grain by our ancient ancestors for the first time that produced a food source that was large enough and stable enough to support permanent settlements .	因為它是我們古老的祖先 , 第一次製造出一種食物來源 , 可以支持永久的生存 。
and if we look at what those settlements were like , we see they were compact .	如果我們看看這些組裝是什麼樣子 , 我們看到它們是相同的 。
they were surrounded by productive farm land and dominated by large temple complexes like this one at ur , that were , in fact , effectively , spiritualized , central food distribution centers .	它們被生產力的農田和中央食物分配中心食物分配中心食物分配中心
because it was the temples that organized the harvest , gathered in the grain , offered it to the gods , and then offered the grain that the gods didn't eat back to the people .	因為它是有機化的海岸 , 帶著上帝 , 帶著上帝 , 再帶上帝 , 不要再吃回來 。
so , if you like , the whole spiritual and physical life of these cities was dominated by the grain and the harvest that sustained them .	所以 , 如果你喜歡 , 整個精神和身體生活 , 那些城市的所有精神和身體生活都被抓住了 。
and in fact , that's true of every ancient city .	事實上 , 每個古老城市都一樣 。
but of course not all of them were that small .	但當然不是所有人都很小 。
famously , rome had about a million citizens by the first century a . d .	很有名的 , 羅馬有一百萬公民 , 羅馬有一百萬公民 。
so how did a city like this feed itself ?	所以 , 像這樣的城市 , 怎麼樣 ?
the answer is what i call " ancient food miles . "	答案是 , 我稱之為 「 古代食物哩 」 。
basically , rome had access to the sea , which made it possible for it to import food from a very long way away .	基本上 , 羅馬在海中得到了它 , 讓它可以從很長的路徑走到海中 。
this is the only way it was possible to do this in the ancient world , because it was very difficult to transport food over roads , which were rough .	這是唯一的方法可以在古老世界中做這件事 , 因為它很難運送食物 , 因為它很難運送食物 , 路上是很困難的 。
and the food obviously went off very quickly .	食物顯然是很快的 。
so rome effectively waged war on places like carthage and egypt just to get its paws on their grain reserves .	所以 , 羅馬效應的戰爭 , 像是卡西和埃及埃及埃及埃及埃及埃及埃及埃及埃及埃及埃及埃及埃及埃及埃及埃及埃及埃及 。
and , in fact , you could say that the expansion of the empire was really sort of one long , drawn out militarized shopping spree , really .	事實上 , 你可以說 , 擴張的擴展是很長的 , 實際上 , 可以說擴張的擴展 , 其實是很長的 , 實際上 , 可以說擴展的擴展是很長的 , 其實是很長的 , 其實是很長的 。
in fact i love the fact , i just have to mention this: rome in fact used to import oysters from london , at one stage . i think that's extraordinary .	事實上 , 我很喜歡這個事實 , 我只需要提到:羅馬其實是來自倫敦的 , 一個階段 , 我想這很不凡 。
so rome shaped its hinterland through its appetite .	所以羅馬形狀它的形狀 。
but the interesting thing is that the other thing also happened in the preindustrial world .	但有趣的是 , 其他事情也發生在工業世界 。
if we look at a map of london in the 17th century , we can see that its grain , which is coming in from the thames , along the bottom of this map .	如果我們看看倫敦的地圖時 , 我們可以看到它的地圖是從十七世紀的地圖 , 來到這裡的地圖 , 我們可以看到它的地圖 。
so the grain markets were to the south of the city .	所以 , 黃金市場是城市的南方 。
and the roads leading up from them to cheapside , which was the main market , were also grain markets .	道路是主要的市場 , 主要市場也是主要市場 , 也是金錢 。
and if you look at the name of one of those streets , bread street , you can tell what was going on there 300 years ago .	如果你看看那些街道的名字 , 你可以說在300年前發生了什麼事 。
and the same of course was true for fish .	當然 , 魚類也是如此 。
fish was , of course , coming in by river as well . same thing .	魚類 , 當然 , 來自河流 , 也是一樣的 。
and of course billingsgate , famously , was london's fish market , operating onsite here until the mid1980s .	當然 , 可是倫敦的魚市場 , 直到1980年代末期 。
which is extraordinary , really , when you think about it .	這很不可思議 , 真的 , 當你想到它的時候 。
everybody else was wandering around with mobile phones that looked like bricks and sort of smelly fish happening down on the port .	每個人都穿著手機 , 看起來像是磚塊 , 看起來像磚塊 , 像磚塊 , 像磚塊一樣 , 看起來像是磚塊 , 看起來像是磚塊 , 像磚塊一樣 。
this is another thing about food in cities: once its roots into the city are established , they very rarely move .	這是另一個關於食物的城市:一旦它根入城市裡 , 它們很罕見 。
meat is a very different story because , of course , animals could walk into the city .	肉是個非常不同的故事 , 當然 , 動物可以走進城市裡 。
so much of london's meat was coming from the northwest , from scotland and wales .	倫敦的肉來自北部 , 來自西北部 , 從蘇格蘭和沃爾斯 。
so it was coming in , and arriving at the city at the northwest , which is why smithfield , london's very famous meat market , was located up there .	所以 , 在北方的那一刻 , 由於西北部的市長 , 這也是為什麼smithfield , 倫敦的巨大的市場 , 在那裡 。
poultry was coming in from east anglia and so on , to the northeast .	北方是來自東東的東方 , 到北方 。
i feel a bit like a weather woman doing this . anyway , and so the birds were coming in with their feet protected with little canvas shoes .	我覺得有點像一位天氣婦女 , 所以鳥類在飛機上飛過來 , 讓鳥類在飛機上飛行 , 讓鳥類在飛機上飛行 。
and then when they hit the eastern end of cheapside , that's where they were sold , which is why it's called poultry .	然後當他們進入東方的東方便宜時 , 他們被告知 , 這就是為什麼它被稱為 「 大屠殺 」 。
and , in fact , if you look at the map of any city built before the industrial age , you can trace food coming in to it .	事實上 , 如果你看看在工業時代的地圖 , 你就可以收集食物來到這裡 。
you can actually see how it was physically shaped by food , both by reading the names of the streets , which give you a lot of clues .	你可以看到它是如何塑造食物 , 透過閱讀街頭的名字 , 讓你們知道它是如何形狀的 。
friday street , in a previous life , is where you went to buy your fish on a friday .	昨天 , 一個星期五的星期五 , 你去買你的魚 。
but also you have to imagine it full of food .	但你必須想像它充滿了食物 。
because the streets and the public spaces were the only places where food was bought and sold .	因為街道和公共空間是唯一的食物被買賣和公共空間 。
and if we look at an image of smithfield in 1830 you can see that it would have been very difficult to live in a city like this and be unaware of where your food came from .	如果我們在1830年看到這張圖片 , 你可以看到它會非常困難地住在一個城市裡 , 像這樣 , 不論你在哪裡 , 可以看到它會非常困難 。
in fact , if you were having sunday lunch , the chances were it was mooing or bleating outside your window about three days earlier .	事實上 , 如果你在星期日午餐時 , 可能是在你的窗戶上 , 大概三天前就出現了 。
so this was obviously an organic city , part of an organic cycle .	這很明顯是有機的機械循環 。
and then 10 years later everything changed .	接著10年後 , 一切改變了 。
this is an image of the great western in 1840 .	這是1840年的圖片 。
and as you can see , some of the earliest train passengers were pigs and sheep .	如你所見 , 一些最早的訓練乘客是豬和羊 。
so all of a sudden , these animals are no longer walking into market .	突然間 , 這些動物不再走進市場 。
they're being slaughtered out of sight and mind , somewhere in the countryside .	他們被奴隸於心中 , 不管在國內的任何地方 。
and they're coming into the city by rail .	他們會進入城市的城市 。
and this changes everything .	這改變了一切 。
to start off with , it makes it possible for the first time to grow cities , really any size and shape , in any place .	首先 , 要開始 , 要開始 , 它會讓它成為可能的第一次成長城市 , 實在任何地方 , 或任何地方 。
cities used to be constrained by geography ; they used to have to get their food through very difficult physical means .	城市被地理被地理所包圍 , 他們習慣要把食物帶到非常困難的身體上 。
all of a sudden they are effectively emancipated from geography .	突然間 , 由地理上有所影響 。
and as you can see from these maps of london , in the 90 years after the trains came , it goes from being a little blob that was quite easy to feed by animals coming in on foot , and so on , to a large splurge , that would be very , very difficult to feed with anybody on foot , either animals or people .	如你所見的 , 在火星上 , 在火星上 , 大約九十年後 , 火星是非常非常困難的 , 可以從這些地圖上 , 到一個大型的水域 , 可以從這些地圖上 , 很容易餵飽動物 , 以此類型 , 牠們會非常非常困難 , 要餵飽動物 , 或人 。
and of course that was just the beginning . after the trains came cars , and really this marks the end of this process .	當然 , 剛剛剛開始的時候 , 火車結束後 , 火車開車之後 , 火車就結束了 。
it's the final emancipation of the city from any apparent relationship with nature at all .	它是整個城市與大自然之間的關係 。
and this is the kind of city that's devoid of smell , devoid of mess , certainly devoid of people , because nobody would have dreamed of walking in such a landscape .	這是一種城市 , 是因為沒有人會在這種城市中 , 因為沒有人會在這種城市中 , 因為沒有人會在這種城市中 , 避免沉默、沉默、沉默 , 因為沒有人會夢想在這個城市中 。
in fact , what they did to get food was they got in their cars , drove to a box somewhere on the outskirts , came back with a week's worth of shopping , and wondered what on earth to do with it .	實際上 , 他們要把食物放在他們的車子上 , 把車子放進去 , 拿到一個盒子 , 到一個盒子 , 到一個盒子 , 到一個盒子 , 到一個盒子 , 到一個盒子 , 到一個盒子 , 到一個盒子 , 到一個盒子 , 到一個盒子 , 到一個盒子 , 到一個盒子 。
and this really is the moment when our relationship , both with food and cities , changes completely .	這是我們的關係 , 食物和城市 , 改變完全不同 。
here we have food that used to be the center , the social core of the city at the periphery .	這裡 , 我們有食物 , 城市的社群 。
it used to be a social event , buying and selling food .	它曾經是社交活動 , 買賣食物 。
we used to cook ; now we just add water , or a little bit of an egg if you're making a cake or something .	我們以前烹煮了 , 只是加入水 , 或一些蛋糕的蛋糕 。
we don't smell food to see if it's okay to eat .	我們不聞食物 , 看看它是否好吃 。
we just read the back of a label on a packet .	我們剛剛讀了一封郵件的背後
and we don't value food . we don't trust it .	我們沒有價值食物 , 我們不相信它 。
so instead of trusting it , we fear it .	所以 , 我們不相信它 , 我們害怕它 。
and instead of valuing it , we throw it away .	而不是評估它 , 我們將它丟掉 。
one of the great ironies of modern food systems is that they've made the very thing they promised to make easier much harder .	現代食品系統的最大量之一就是他們讓自己變得更加困難 。
by making it possible to build cities anywhere and any place , they've actually distanced us from our most important relationship , which is that of us and nature .	為了讓它能建立城市 , 或任何地方 , 都能在我們與大自然中建立城市 。
and also they've made us dependent on systems that only they can deliver , that , as we've seen , are unsustainable .	同時 , 他們也讓我們依賴系統 , 只能提供我們所看到的 , 不穩定的 。
so what are we going to do about that ?	我們要怎麼做呢 ?
it's not a new question .	這不是一個新的問題 。
500 years ago it's what thomas more was asking himself .	五百年前 , 湯瑪斯會問自己自己 。
this is the frontispiece of his book " utopia . "	這是他的書《烏托邦》 。

utopia was actually a word that thomas moore used deliberately .	烏托邦其實是thomasmoore使用的詞 。

weeks from the charter for compassion launch , karen armstrong looks at religion's role in the 21st century: will its dogmas divide us ? or will it unite us for common good ? she reviews the catalysts that can drive the world's faiths to rediscover the golden rule .	四週後 , 卡拉斯特在21世紀末期的教訓是:將它的信仰轉換成黃金規則 , 可以讓世界的信仰轉換成目標 , 可以讓世界的信仰轉換成目標 , 可以讓世界的信仰轉換成金條規則 。
god , ted prize , global issues , politics , religion , tedglobal2009 , violence	上帝 , 全球議題 , 政治 , 宗教 , ted , 全球議題 , 政治 , 宗教 , 209年 , 伊斯蘭國 。
karen armstrong: let's revive the golden rule	克里斯蒂:讓我們重新維持黃金規則 。
for years i've been feeling frustrated , because as a religious historian , i've become acutely aware of the centrality of compassion in all the major world faiths .	多年來 , 我變得很沮喪 , 因為身為宗教歷史學家 , 我一直感到沮喪 , 因為身為宗教歷史學家 , 我已經變得很沮喪 , 因為身為宗教歷史學家 , 我一直感到沮喪 。
every single one of them has evolved their own version of what's been called the golden rule .	每一個人都演化出自己的版本 , 叫做黃金規則 。
sometimes it comes in a positive version " always treat all others as you'd like to be treated yourself . "	有時 , 正面版本是 「 總是對待你自己 」 的正面版本 。
and equally important is the negative version " don't do to others what you would not like them to do to you . "	同樣重要的是負面版本: 「 別對其他人做你不喜歡他們做的事 。 」
look into your own heart , discover what it is that gives you pain and then refuse , under any circumstance whatsoever , to inflict that pain on anybody else .	看看你的心臟 , 發現它是什麼樣子 , 讓你痛苦 , 並且拒絕 , 在任何情況下 , 在任何情況下 , 會讓你痛苦 , 並且拒絕 , 在任何情況下 , 在任何情況下 , 讓疼痛受傷 。
and people have emphasized the importance of compassion , not just because it sounds good , but because it works .	人們對同情心的重要性 , 不僅是因為它聽起來很好 , 但是因為它的重要性 。
people have found that when they have implemented the golden rule as confucius said , " all day and every day , " not just a question of doing your good deed for the day and then returning to a life of greed and egotism , but to do it all day and every day , you dethrone yourself from the center of your world , put another there , and you transcend yourself .	人們發現 , 當他們被提到 「 日常生活 」 和 「 所有日子 」 時 , 每一天 , 都會把你自己放進去 , 把自己放進去 , 把自己放進去 , 把自己放進去 , 把自己放進去 , 把自己放進去 , 把自己放進去 。
and it brings you into the presence of what's been called god , nirvana , rama , tao .	它將你帶到我們所謂的 「 神 」 、 「 神 」 、 「 神 」 、 「 神 」 、 「 神 」 、 「 神 」 。
something that goes beyond what we know in our egobound existence .	在我們所知的事物中 , 我們所知的一切都存在 。
but you know you'd never know it a lot of the time , that this was so central to the religious life .	但你知道你永遠不會知道 , 這太過了很多時間 , 這就是宗教生活的中心 。
because with a few wonderful exceptions , very often when religious people come together , religious leaders come together , they're arguing about abstruse doctrines or uttering a council of hatred or inveighing against homosexuality or something of that sort .	因為有一些很棒的例子 , 宗教領袖聚集在一起 , 宗教領袖聚集在一起 , 宗教領袖聚集在一起 , 宗教領袖聚集在一起 , 宗教領袖聚集在一起 , 宗教領袖聚集在一起 , 宗教領袖聚集在一起 , 宗教領袖聚集在一起 , 宗教領袖聚集在一起 , 宗教領袖聚集在一起 , 宗教領袖聚集在一起 , 宗教領袖聚集在一起 , 宗教領袖聚集在一起 , 宗教領袖聚集在一起 , 宗教領袖聚集在一起 , 宗教領袖聚集在一起 , 宗教領袖聚在一起 , 宗教領袖聚集在一起 , 認同
often people don't really want to be compassionate .	通常人們並不想同情心 。
i sometimes see when i'm speaking to a congregation of religious people a sort of mutinous expression crossing their faces because people often want to be right instead .	我有時會看到當我說話時 , 人們常常想對抗拒絕 , 因為人們常常想對抗拒絕 。

now why was i so grateful to ted ?	為什麼我這麼感謝ted ?
because they took me very gently from my booklined study and brought me into the 21st century , enabling me to speak to a much , much wider audience than i could have ever conceived .	因為他們把我帶到21世紀 , 讓我能從我的書線上學習 , 並帶我到21世紀 , 讓我能更廣泛的觀眾 。

if we don't manage to implement the golden rule globally , so that we treat all peoples , wherever and whoever they may be , as though they were as important as ourselves , i doubt that we'll have a viable world to hand on to the next generation .	如果我們不管制定規則 , 那麼我們對所有人的信任 , 無論他們是誰 , 無論他們是誰 , 無論他們是誰 , 無論他們是誰 , 無論他們是誰 , 無論他們是誰 , 無論他們是誰 , 無論他們是誰 , 無論他們是誰 , 無論他們是誰 , 無論他們是誰 , 無論他們是誰 , 無論他們是誰 ,
the task of our time , one of the great tasks of our time , is to build a global society , as i said , where people can live together in peace .	我們時間的任務之一 , 就是建立一個全球社會 , 如我所說 , 人們可以住在和平 。
and the religions that should be making a major contribution are instead seen as part of the problem .	宗教應該要做出一個主要的貢獻 , 而不是被視為是問題的一部分 。
and of course it's not just religious people who believe in the golden rule .	當然 , 不只是宗教信仰在黃金法則 。

that is the torah and everything else is only commentary . "	也是唯一的評論 。 」
and the rabbis and the early fathers of the church who said that any interpretation of scripture that bred hatred and disdain was illegitimate .	拉比和早期的父親教堂說 , 教堂的文字是非法的 , 不論是非法的 。

in malaysia , there is going to be an art exhibition in which leading artists are going to be taking people , young people , and showing them that compassion also lies at the root of all art .	在馬拉雅 , 讓藝術展現了藝術展覽 , 讓藝術展現了藝術的展覽 , 讓藝術展現了藝術展覽 , 讓藝術展現出藝術展展 , 讓藝術展現出同情心 , 讓藝術展現出同情心的藝術作品 。

but it can't stop there . it can't stop with the launch .	但它無法停止 , 無法停止 , 無法停止 。
religious teaching , this is where we've gone so wrong , concentrating solely on believing abstruse doctrines .	宗教教學 , 我們已經走錯了 , 以致於信仰的教義 。
